police even helped me get into the spot I found after circling for an 
hour :-) ) The only negative moment was when I spotted 5 very healthy 
appearing people get out of a shiny new car parked in a Handicapped spot.

know,  but IMHO, if you're not truly handicapped, placard or not, you

Subject: EarthSpace in Seattle
To: sfraves@techno
Date: Wed, 1 Jun 1994 13:24:49 -0700 (PDT)
X-Mailer: ELM [version 2.4 PL23]
Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=US-ASCII

Content-Length: 3183      
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno

EarthSpace
Seattle 5/28/94

We arrived at 10:30pm and were among the first 30 or so people.
The site was 45 minutes northeast of Seattle - a huge meadow
surrounded by trees, hills and streams.  The weather was drizzly
and chilly but the enthusiasm was clear.  Notable planning and
consideration were put into this party.  Two main sound areas,
a chill tent and a food pavilion.  The main sound system was
already running with Shocka from Portland at the helm.  For some
reason (intuition), I danced lunatish from the getgo while friends
gathered at one of several fires (olts of wood on hand).  A steady
stream of people kept the energy rising, and a few dozen people
were dancing in the wet grass as Jon Howard took over, though the 
majority were sticking near the fires.

Things started going a little wrong when the two main sound stacks 
failed around 12:30, remaining intermittent for the next hour or
two.  Fortunately, there was a third tower set out from the main
dance area and its fire which carried on.  I would say the party
peaked between 2 and 3:30 when there was a small but definite rave
happening by these working speakers, and we had the longest period
of no rain.  Major thrill as this group hooted and jumped through
a favorite song of mine I can only identify as "Never Gonna Let It
Get Me Down."  What a jam!!

Masa from Seattle was calmly kicking the butt of unhapiness when I
noticed the main speakers were working, so we moved around the fire
to the front again.  But with everyone (moving) still on the other
side, we were quickly drawn back.  Then someone got on the P.A. and
asked everyone to please come and share their energy with Masa.  
This was cool, as a lot of people responded, including those who 
had not been dancing before.

Things were totally groovy at this point, around 3:45, with about
half of the estimated 300 people there hanging near the sound. Then
disaster struck.  The sound cut off, and someone came on the P.A.
saying "The police are here.  Seems the sound can be heard by a
neighbor a mile away, which is a good thing if you happen to like
house music, but not a good thing if you don't happen to like 
house music.  We're on private land, so we don't have to leave, 
but we can't resume the beat till 9am.  Everyone hang while we 
figure out what to do."

We warmed by a fire while people conferenced.  It was decided by 
the group mind (yes!) to wait it out rather than try to move the
party.  It was getting light when we moved to the chill tent.  This
ended up being the highlight of the experience for me, as about 20
people lying under and on a tarp enjoyed the fantastic psychedelic
ambient music, the pouring rain and the marvelous green.  It was
one of those times when I realize again why we sometimes jump 
through such big hoops to end up in scenes like this.

We left around 7am, as some in our group were pretty shagged.  It
seemed at least a hundred or so were still there as we left.  I 
been told earlier that Dub Tribe was going to play for two and a
half hours, but I don't know if they did.  The sun broke through
as we drove home, so I'm optimistic that the faithful were treated
to a beautiful morning.

	Wow, that's quite the middle name.. :)  I know exactly what you
mean, though.  That's really cool to give us a listing of the tracks
you play, because a lot of djs, even though they might not tape their
labels, sort of try to keep their music a secret.  I don't live in
sf, but I must say, you delve into some pretty hard trance compared
to the "popular" underground music on the west coast.  This is a
great thing.  Progressive house and progressive trance are my
favorite types of music, but I have a lot of respect for DJs that
stay true to the underground.  I'm not saying that all the big name
DJs (wicked posse, etc) aren't 'underground', but when you hear the
same high energy house all the time it can become almost like 'top
40'.  Just for an example, how many of you could hum or sing 2 fatt
guitars on a moments notice?  Even though people might pester you to
play house, or to play music that they can get into more, I really
enjoy a DJ that has a _unique_, experimental style.  Some people just
aren't open-minded enough.  Variety is good in all things :)

Luke

Here's something that came from alt.drugs: the address of a testing lab. Many of
you have probably seen it before (anyone actually use it? Let us know...).

>>S.P. Lab, 55426 N.W. 79th Avenue, Miami, Florida 33166.  They
>>      ask for a sample wrapped in foil or plastic, enclosed in an
>>      envolope, with a slip of paper telling the alleged content,
>>      cost, any undesirable side-effects noticed, $25.00 per sample,
>>      and a five-digit number to identify the sample.  After 14 days,
>>      call (305) 757-2566 for the result.

Of course, if you already shelled out the $ for the drug itself, shelling out
more to find out if it was what it was sold as is annoying, to say the least.
Too bad dealers (or the makers) can't be more honest. Any honest dealers out
there?

Brian

hi all, 
        this is just to let you know of the california hemp fest this
saturday June 4th.  It is at the bandshell in golden gate park and it's
free.  Live entertainment by Fishbone, Fungo Mungo, Total Devastation, DJ
Markie Mark ( full moon ), Asphalt Poetry and the Marginal Profits. There
is also going to be a lot of different booths by hemp importers, retailers
and producers etc.  The event is put on by The Cannabis Action Network and
High Times Magazine.  Communion will have a booth with a small sound system
and dj's josh, galen and markie.  It starts at noon and go's to 6pm.
        That night I am putting on a party to celebrate the festival and
the 20th anniversary of high times. There will be 4 bands there, a fusion
of hip hop, acid  jazz, funk and rap. House will be provided by markie
mark, tony and bam bam.  Markie will be playing an obscure set of different
music to fuse from the bands to the dj's.  This event has a lot of
potential.  We are making an attempt at integration, by exposing  different
cultures of peoples to the same experience.  I believe a lot of cultures
are portraying a similar message, going the same direction, we are just on
different paths.  I deeply believe in the rave culture, but we alone are
not going to bring about enough change to sustain the survival of humanity.
 Integration of like minded peoples into a global consciousness of
community is the only way forward.  
info  415 267 4800
$5 18 & over, no alcohol, all profits to cannabis action network 
respects
Martin O Brien

On Wed, 1 Jun 1994, Grey Six wrote:

> party.  It was getting light when we moved to the chill tent.  This
> ended up being the highlight of the experience for me, as about 20
> people lying under and on a tarp enjoyed the fantastic psychedelic
> ambient music, the pouring rain and the marvelous green.  It was
> one of those times when I realize again why we sometimes jump 
> through such big hoops to end up in scenes like this.
Well, thank you! :-)  I was pretty bummed when they had to shut down the 
sound system, we thought we were far enough out there to not cause any 
problems... oh well... I played for the first 2 1/2 hours of "the long 
noiseless period" in the ambient tent and I could really feel that 
everyone in the tent was well-immersed.  I'm glad you had an enjoyable 
time in there, because I sure did... I was worried that ambient music 
would never be seen in high regard in this area, but I'd like to thank 
the Choc-Lit Factory and especially Ethan for seeing that the ambient DJs 
got a nice tent and a wonderful sound system.  With no bleed from the 
main system and an interested crowd, I'd have to say that Earthspace was 
the best site I've ever played on.  It's really hard to articulate how it 
feels to play for the sunrise.. it's just brilliant.

Peace,
Matt Corwine

disabilities" that are not readily apparent to the ignorant. I myself 
quit using my placard (and I've regretted it) because of dirty looks from 
people who I guess just don't know any better. So basically, I decided 
that even though I have a very painful messed up foot and profound 
inner-ear damage (I get disoriented very easily) and asstd. other health 
problems, I got so sick of being the target of nasty vibes and worse 
looks that I just don't bother to get another one, even though I am 
legally entitled to it. (now you all know why I hardly ever dance and 
don't stay late and stumble around like a drunk when it's dark) :)

Thanks for letting me get that off my chest... :)

VERY GOOD NEWS FOR The Sisters and SFR folks

   Here is some interesting info for you...   It turns out that the
Kennell Club at 628 Divisidero has just turned under new ownership,  and
I had a very long and most interesting meeting with these folks.   We all
sat around the bar (Drinks complimentary),  and discussed some pretty 
amazing new concepts.   Details to follow later.....

   They plan to call their club "The Crash Palace",  and will be featuring
a large variaty of entertainment groups.    This also includes raves,  but
right now,  they are fighting noise complaints from their former tenants,
and work is being done to contain the noise problem,  and build a better
repiour with their neighbors.   

   They started asking me questions about how to set up the dance area,
I suggested they put in some floor fans.    When I suggested what kinds 
of fans were needed in the dance area,  they asked me where to get them,
and sincerely intend to make things much better.    

   When I mentioned that the Sisters needed a space for their parties, 
they said that as long as it wasn't EVERY WEEK,  the Sisters would be
invited to use the space.    They are also amienable to holding SFR
parties,  Basics,  or any Martin o Brian production,   but held
some reservation about having a WICKED held there.

   The space is fantastic,  if you haven't been there.    It is primarily
one large space,   high ceilings,   and well ventilated.    

John D.

Maui-Your Sister's House said:
> 
> Are you referring to the stuff that has made two of my friends quite 
> sick? It takes about 9 hrs. to go away and is profoundly dysphoric.

Here's the entry from Pihkal,  check the duration. Its a doozy.

DOB; 2,5-DIMETHOXY-4-BROMOAMPHETAMINE

DOSAGE: 1.0 - 3.0 mg. (which is a really small amount)

DURATION: 18 - 30 h. 
	  ~~~~~~~~~
	  ~~~~~~~~~


QUALITATIVE COMMENTS: (with 0.4 mg) There was a distinct enhancement
of visual perception, and some strengthening of colors.  A clean, cold
feeling of wind on the skin.  I felt an enriched emotional affect, a
comfortable and good feeling, and easy sleeping with colorful and
important dreams.

(with 2.0 mg) There was a continuous tremor at the physical level,
and an incredible Moebius strip representation of reality at the
intellectual level.  I was able to enter into personal problems
easily, and get out again when I chose to.  During the next day, there
were brief lapses of attention, or little fugue states, and it was not
until the following evening that I was completely myself again.

(with 2.8 mg) About three hours into this I had a severe cramp, and
had a near fainting response to the pain, and yet there was no pain!
I felt that I was very near a loss of consciousness, and this was most
disturbing.  There were flashes of depersonalization.  I saw rings
around the moon with prismatic colors, and there were long-lasting
Rafter-imagesS following any viewings of points of light.  I was still
a good plus 1 at 14 hours, but did manage to sleep.  It was the next
day before I was again at baseline.

(with 3.0 mg) This was a complex, but a very good day.  It involved
making a large pot of chicken-vegetable soup, and listening to H.L.,
my favorite Saturday morning fundamentalist Christian radio preacher,
bless Tim.  The Democrats are not exactly all anti-American dupes of
Moscow (or the Devil), but to H.L., they are practically, almost,
next-door to it.  The Rapture is supposed to happen tomorrow according
to a certain book, newly published (just in time, looks like) and he
is busy softening the possible disappointment of those who may find
themselves unchanged Monday morning.  Wunnerful.  It's been one heck
of a good experiment, and I canUt understand why we waited nine years
to try this gorgeous stuff.  Without going into the cosmic and
delicious details, let's just say itUs a great material and a good
level.

(with 0.5 mg of the RRS isomer) I am underway, and this is a smooth
intoxication.  I am completely functional, but still really a plus
two.  I would not choose to drive a car.  Not very far.  I felt a
rather quick dropping to a plus-one at the fifth hour, but there is a
residual stimulation still the following morning.

(with 1.0 mg of the RRS isomer) By the fourth hour I am absolutely a
+++ and am searching the kitchen for food.  But what I eat is only
so-so.  There is not the introspection or intensity of 2.0 milligrams
of the racemate material, but this is a rewarding place nonethless.
At the 18th hour, there was some fitful sleep, with bizarre dreams.
The next day I was still hungry for altered spaces, and successfully
challenged the residual plus one with LSD and, as is usually the case,
acid cut right through the detritus and allowed a direct shot up to a
+++ again.

(with 1.5 mg of the RRS isomer) This is a +++ but it is vaguely
irrational.  I feel a heavy body load, but then the temperature
outside is over a hundred degrees and I may not be in the best of all
physical environments.  I would not wish any higher dosage.  There
were cat-naps at the twelth hour, but most symptoms were still there
at the 18th hour.  A good experience.  It would be interesting to
compare this, some day, with 3.0 milligrams of the racemate.

(with 0.5 mg of the RSS isomer) There are no effects at all.

(with 1.0 mg of the RSS isomer) There is something warm and nice at a
couple of hours into this, but I am no more than threshold, and the
effects are very slight.  By the fifth hour there are no longer any
effects.

EXTENSIONS AND COMMENTARY: The stars had clearly lined up in favor of
making DOB and exploring its biological activity.  This preparation
had been completed in 1967 and the report of this compound and its
unprecedently high potency published in 1971.  And very shortly, two
additional papers appeared completely independently.  One described
DOB made via a different route, and describing high activity in rats.
The other described DOB and a couple of closely related brominated
amphetamines and their action in man.

This is one of the last of the experimental compounds within the
phenethylamine family on which any animal toxicity studies were
performed by me prior to human studies.  A mouse injected with 50
mg/Kg (ip) showed considerable twitching and was irritable.  Another,
at 100 mg/Kg (ip), had overt shaking at 20 minutes, which evolved into
persistent hyperactivity that lasted several hours.  Yet another, at
125 mg/Kg (ip), lost much of her righting reflex within 15 minutes,
entered into convulsions at 50 minutes, and was dead a half hour
later.  A fourth mouse, at 150 mg/Kg (ip), entered into spontaneous
convulsions within 10 minutes, and expired in what looked like an
uncomfortable death at 22 minutes following injection.  What was
learned?  That the LD/50 was somewhere between 100 and 125 mg/Kg for
the mouse.  And an effective dose in man of maybe 2 mg (for an 80 Kg
man) is equivalent to 25 ug/Kg.  Therefore the index of safety (the
therapeutic index, the lethal dose divided by the effective dose) is
well over a thousand.  I feel that two mice were killed without
anything of value having been received in return.

Actually, it is very likely that the damaging, if not lethal, level of
DOB in man is a lot lower than this ratio would imply.  There was a
report of a death of a young lady following the snorting of an amount
of DOB so massive, there was the actual recovery of over nine
milligrams of the drug from her body tissues in the post-mortem
examination.  It was said that she and her companion had thought that
the drug they were using was MDA and, taking a dosage appropriate for
this, effectively overdosed themselves.  He survived, following
convulsions and an extended period (several weeks) of being in a
comatose state.  Tragic examples have been reported that involve
arterial vascular spasm.  But in most overdose cases ascribed to DOB,
the identity of the drug has remained unestablished.

As with DOI, the presence of a heavy atom, the bromine atom, in DOB
makes the radioactive isotope labelled material a powerful research
tool.  Studies with DOB labelled with either 82Br or 77Br have been
used in human subjects to follow the distribution of the drug.  The
use of a whole body scanner permits the imaging of the intact body,
with the travelings of the radioactivity easily followed from outside.
A fascinating finding is that DOB goes first and foremost to the human
lung where it accumulates for a couple of hours.  It is only
afterwards that the brain level builds up.  There is a strong
implication that some metabolic conversion occurs in the lung, and it
is only after this that the truly active metabolite is available for
central action.  This is consistent with the relatively slow onset of
effect, and the very long duration of action.

As with all the other psychedelics which can and have been studied as
their optical isomers, it is the RRS isomer of DOB that is the more
active than the racemic mixture, and the RSS is certainly much less
active, but it has never been run up to fully active levels.  The
alpha-ethyl homologue of DOB is mentioned under ARIADNE.  The
positionally rearranged isomers of DOB are discussed under META-DOB.




 ,
dana

okay-seems there  is something dodgy going around pretending to be e.  It 
is definately psychoactive, but it's difficult to describe exactly what 
it is that it's doing.  You are high-you feel strange.  Sounds are 
intensified.  It isn't a touchy-feely thing 
(definately not e).  And yes, it lasted for over 20 hours.  DOB is 2,5 
Dimethoxy-4-bromoamphetamine.  It can be eaten or snorted and the 
recommended dosage is .5mg - 1mg.  50mg is an OD.  It can ccause 
vasoconstriction of the extremities which can result in gangrene and loss 
of limbs.  Onset: 1-2 hours
           Plateau: 8-12 hours   
           Baseline: 16-18 hours
it causes no loss of lucidity-it keeps you awake-but sitting and tripping 
on nothing very stimulating or interesting.  Our sense was "Yeah, we're 
tripping.  We feel funny.  So What!"  For us this drug held no 



 
enlightenment-no magick.  That might have had a lot to do with the 
environment we were in.  We began enjoying ourselves when we were out of 
the club environment.  Sounds had a powerful layered quality--and both of 
us found that we were extremely sensitive to the unconscious body 
language that people used.  It was as if a lot of people were 
caricatures instead of actual human beings.  Maybe it wasn't DOB.  We 
thought it was 2CB for awhile-but it lasted too long and there was no sex 
vibe present-which I've heard is present in 2CB.  Oh well, go figure.
Know it's out there-beware means BE AWARE.
peace love and lots of joy
michelle

DOB--I think--Okay, we were given these white tablets that looked like 
oversized aspirin--horsepills.  Ever eat a big fat codeine?  It looked 
(and tasted) a lot like that.  I don't remember there being any numbers 
or distinguishing marks on the pills -- but they could have been there.  
I made the purchase from someone who hasn't let me down in 2 1/2 years.  
Took him by suprise as well.  Good luck kiddies.
peace love joy,
michelle

also, please remember that when you call those numbers, they have your
phone number, by virtue of it being an 800 number. if they pay for it
they somehow have a right to know who called.

so, if you're paranoid enough, you can find reasons to be uneasy w/
numbers being distributed on lists such as sfr, and then having various
marketeers/spooks 'n' weenies adding another correlation between you
and your number and your interests.

just last week, i called a very strange number from MCI that someone
had posted by e-mail -- i was piqued with the description "looks like
MCI has lost it" so I called to find out about what the weirdness was.
That evening, I got a call from MCI asking whether I wanted to switch
to their service, and I have never gotten a call from MCI before. Could
be coincidence, but I doubt it.

Hi Everyone,

I am writing what will soon be a quarterly club and event guide for the West
Coast for a house music industry magazine called Underground News. It's going
to be a very small (too small) sampler of nightlife in several U.S. and 
International cities printed in an insert booklet intended for people to
pull out and take with them on vacations.  My job is to describe around
10 or so places in each city that I would take someone to if they were only
visiting for a short time.  I would like it to be a better representation
than just the places that I think are cool because let's face it, I don't
necessarily know where the real cool places are.  I am asking for your
input - if you could name off 5-10 clubs that you like to attend in your
area and perhaps one or two reasons why (space, vibe, DJs, price, whatever).
Additionally, I am interested in those local haunts for food, coffee, 
drinking or just unique nightlife. To give you an idea of what I have started
with, these are some of the clubs that I will probably talk about:

Los Angeles

Brass
Public Space
Moontribe events (don't worry guys, no phone number!!)
Sketch Pad
Respect
Sweet Sundays
Parliament
Small Factory of Sound
Ambient Lounge

San Francisco

Come-Unity
Wicked
SPAZ
Spundae
Spiral Jive
Pepper
Organic
Test

If there are serious objections to any of those, I would love to hear it as
well. I am going to mention sfraves and socal-raves as invaluable resources
in learning about events, and perhaps give the (calendar-only?) addresses? Do
you think this is a good idea. Please forgive all of the questions and please
do take the time to let me know what  your favorite spots are!

Thanks,


Tamara


P.S. I guess I will also be doing radio too but I think I've got that covered...

ISSUE number -2- of the OFFICIAL
 
** Zippy Pronoia Tour to America Electronic Newsletter **
______________________________________________
 
PRONOIA:  The sneaking suspicion that someone is conspiring
behind your back to help you, AND YOU THEM!
 
*****  The border between the REAL and the UNREAL is NOT FIXED.
It merely marks the last place where rival shamans fought each other
to a stalemate.  *****   -Robert Anton Wilson
 
To subscribe / submit questions or feedback,
please e-mail the editor: cubensis@well.sf.ca.us
______________________________________________
 
CONTENTS:
 
1-  a note from the editor
2-  The Whole Earth Lectronic Link (WELL) feedback
3-  some zippy personalities
4-  projects
5-  more soy sauce needed
6-  tour announcements
______________________________________________
 
1-  a note from the editor---
 
Dear fellow pronoids--
 
As one of our rainbow netweavers recently said, life is a resource to
discover, not a problem to be solved.  A pattern is emerging from deep
within the chaos, and when it finally gels into something recognisable, the
cultural virus will be on a forever-groove.
 
When I last saw Fraser Clark, he was warbling a melody with Lady Miss Kier
of Deee-Lite over the phone: ...people are conspiring to he-e-e-e-elp
you...!
 
The net is being woven in increasingly strange and wonderful patterns, and
if one of the patterns should suddenly shift while still on the loom,
please
forgive and realize the nature of chaos is... well, chaotic.
 
On THAT NOTE, there is a Major Change in the tour schedule (Item 5),
specifically, the first gig.  The NASA event fizzled, no fault of the
Zippies!  But, we must have ashes from which a phoenix can arise... so a
HUGE loving welcome to the crew at Liquid Sky in New York City.  The reggae
gig we have been invited to will not be a BIG ZIPPY EVENT, but it will be a
meeting of the subcultures, and a hell of a good jam, mon.
 
The next newsletter will be written from the steaming bowels of New York
City.  Look for the butterfly squirming from the core of a rotting apple...
 
 
       -cubensis
_________________
 
2-  The Whole Earth Lectronic Link (WELL) feedback
 
Q:   What do you call one zippy walking down the street?
A:   A virtual riot.
 
On the WELL, in the g house conference, the topic The Zippies has surpassed
the 100-person mark.  Linked to topics in g wired and fringeware, we have
been seeing some *sirius* personalities appear to give their two cents.
>From famous cyberpunk science fiction authors, to underground zine
editors,
to granola-munching rainbow warriors---  the Cyber-tour has been underway
for weeks.  Thanks to all who are participating in this and other areas of
the NET (like alt.rainbow, alt.rave).  The tour is much more empowered due
to the honest dialogue in these virtual communities.  Special thanks to M
Normal, the hostess of g house.
_________________
 
3-  some zippy personalities
 
Everybodys got something to hide, cept for me and my monkey.
                              -Lennon/McCartney
 
What the- who are those strange people looking befuddled at the hustle of
Times Square?  Are they tourists?  Are they extra-terrestrials?  Are they
Illuminati agents?  No, theyre pale Brits with colourful clothes and BIG
attitudes.
 
Fraser Clark, Igniter of tinder---  From the recesses of your foggy 60s
memories, here comes the blond Scotsman sporting a perprtual grin, giving
hugs to all.  From his mouth flows the rolling language of the Zippy
spokesperson extraordinaire-- the promoter of the Megatripolis club in
London--- the editor of Encyclopaedia Psychedelica.
 
Angus Dunwoodydun, the Tech Czar---  Fresh from mixing the live feed of MTV
Europe in the new all-digital studios in London, its the director and
producer of the official zippy documentary film.  Look out for his low-key
delivery and incredible resourcefulness.  Remember to smile for the camera!
 
Catriona Morgan (Kate), the Welsh Weaverwoman---   If she doesnt look right
at you during a conversation, thats ok-  shes probably writing a verbatim
transcript in her little day-planner book.  Tour management never looked so
zippy.  Shes the one negotiating with the Buddhist accountant.
 
...more to come...
_________________
 
4-  projects
 
We are currently working out details for the following projects:
 
--- a downloadable FTP file for access to daily Zippy announcements
        (possibly audio and video will be available)
--- a series of live teleconferences during the summer-- the Zippy
        Pronoia Tour in America with festivals in Germany and the UK
--- cable television updates on specific programming
 
details to follow as they congeal
_________________

This is my first post!  I have been observing the list for a few
months and I just wanted to comment on the SRL show.  Except for the
waiting and the conterfit tickets that messed things up, the show was
really good.  I saw the one 5 years ago in SF and although it was
interesting I couldn't see anything up close.  The show 5 years ago
was held under a freeway overpass and the sonic booms were defening!
I was glad that they had to forsight to pass out ear plugs for this
show.  The SRL people tried to cram everybody in- even the extras but
I guess the fire marshal wouldn't allow it.  The highlight was the
Lightening generator!  There was a giant dinasour like machine, a
sonic canon that spit fire.  a walking cat like machine, multiple
flame machines, a giant spinning top that had neon letters all over
it.  a "Last Supper" effigy that was burned to a crisp. Noise, smoke
and machines.  They did well!  It is very hard to describe the overall
effect, but I enjoyed the show.  Try downloading from the SRL archive
for some cool pictures!  anonymous ftp srl.org if you want them.

                                             Mr Klinik

P.S. does anyone know where Earthspace was at?  Was it in Seattle?

like that.

Thanks Matt/Jess/GreySix; it was a really fun way to celebrate XLR8R, 
which has connected us with each other all over everywhere and given us 
all a forum through which to say some of the things that we feel need 
to be said...

Thanks and props to all of _you_ who came out ready to go for it 
despite the inclement weather conditions (which in some ways worked out 
beautifully; did anyone get a really long look at the suspended 
raindrops in the cone of the laser?) and the relentless hassle by bored 
King County police.  All of us who worked the party were really glad to 
be there handling the little details whilst all of the rest of you 
cooked up a phaaat vibe.  Hope that everyone got a chance to hang out 
around one of the bonfires (especially on the beach) and talk with 
someone they'd never met before.

I'd say that there are definitely more outside events in store for all 
of us, and once the weather becomes reliably nice...<whew>...

Peace!  And Love to you all...

Rhythm&BASS!

Prozactacoatl and Co:

I went to the bandshell for the into the light ravelet last Sat for a few
minutes. The mix was pleasant but too bad about the dust; at any rate a
wunnerful way to spend a Sat afternoon.  

I was curious about my own peripheral participation at the event, that is:
some artwork of mine was printed in the Whole Earth Review and I have
hundreds of comp copies to give away.  I brought ten to the lit table at the
bandshell, and put them down.  Before they hit the table 4 or 5 inquiring
types grabbed e each (after hearing the magic word FREE). I had to leave
soon, and there were still a couple on the table when I left.

So my question is, did getting a magazine like the WER free make their day?
Or were they just discarded later? To me it would seem like free stuff at a
free event is in keeping with the general vibe.  

On a vaguely related note, are there ra scene fanzines that are not A) gig
listings or B) glossy 5 dollar fashion/nightlife coverage?  like for
instance, xeroxed or color artwork and writing like one would find in most
fanzines.  It would seem with the graphics available via ftp and the ones
used on all those handbills such a thing would exist. The only zine I have
seen like that would be Jason Koehn's "The Imaginal Rave", but he only did
one and then moved away. (It had an orange cover with a woman dancing on top
of a swirl, the inside was a rant positing raves as potential
mind-liberating Dionysian revels of good cheer, etc, etc.) Does anyone
indulge in computer graphics outside of making advertisements?


Yr time and consideration ti this matter would be greatly appreciated :)


PHL
lollar@cardio.ucsf.edu

> I understand handicapped placards can also be bought for approx 50 dollars
> at flea markets, if you snoop around enough.  I read this in I believe the
> Chronicle months ago.

Well, the Chronicle is 99% garbage anyway. The fact is, CA has for some 
reason decided that it's more important to crack down on illegal placards 
than it is to arrest rapists, child molesters, etc. This does *NOT* mean 
I condone illegal use of disabled parking! I have "keyed" many a car 
owned by callous jerks who abused these spots.
I'm sure that "black" market placards are out there (seeing as you can 
get a *green card* so easily [supposedly]) but I don't believe them to be 
nearly the problem the news would have you believe.

Any way, let's move on to more fruitful topics-- like, let's talk about 
making sure our parties are fully accessible, and other productive things.

One thing that has definitely kept me from going to events is knowing I 
won't be able to *sit down* near the main area. Who wants to be limited 
to the chill-out room?
I would like for all of us that give/assist parties to try to remember to 
bring some kind of thing for people to sit on-- even if it is just a old  
comforter or whatever. It would encourage more folks to come out. :)

Okay, 'nuff said by me....

Peace!

Maui

hiya all...i am in dc again for vacation! and have been partying my tush off..
(in fact what is sleep? crunch maybe you can explain (: ) as you guys know i
run the dcraves list *dcraves@american.edu* (shameless plug) and the net-ravers
have a nice little scene going on here...

on thursday night, lonnie (ultraworld) my favorite promoter in the *world*
held a party called "rave the bay" (a take off on save the bay) on a boat in 
baltimore harbor all night long...3 decks of music...first floor was breaks
(with our fellow netraver dieselboy) and some trance...second floor wink with some get this housey stuff (house in the east coast...i can't explain it either)
and some ambient/acidjazz/jazz on the top deck...

 needless to say it was amazing to dance the sun up on a boat...and they netraver posse was in full effect...about 20 or so...free lays were given out as we got on the boat (and as dan said "gee i never got laid on a boat" har har)
and after lonnie handed out neato bumper stickers...it was really good to see
the happening scene in dc after reading about hoaxes like pleasuer dome and
the tripotronic parties....

tonight we have rented speakers and are holding a renegade somewhere (hey location to be announced (: ) and people are driving in from phili and stuff...
*3-8 hour drives are nothing for ne-ravers to go to a party*

so i am having a fantastic time...(but i will be home soon)

partyon...susie(:

progressive house than deep house.  That's reserved more for the clubs.

yes it is time again for susie's annual ravers voting guide...

the election is from 7 am to 8 pm on june 7th

here are some interesting issues in san francisco to think about...
 
prop d "Shall the city be required to employ a minimum of 1.971 full duty 
police officers, with an emphasis on assigning officers to neighborhood 
policing an patrol?"

personally, i don't remember how i voted on this issue (absentee) but i 
just wanted to remind people that it is the police who break up our 
parties...and who knows maybe a community based officer would be nicer????

prop i "Shall the City be required to take all actions necessary to 
extend BART services into the Airport terminal area, and shall the 
Airports Commission be required to  take all apporpriate actions to 
generate the revenue necessary for this BARt extension, which shall 
include using any available Airport, regional, state, and federal funds, 
and if necessary, adopting a passenger facility charge, if approved by 
the federal government?"

personally, i say vote YES on this issue so all those ne-ravers who come 
out here don't have to ask cindy and laura for rides all the time (:

just a few thoughts...susie (:

i just wanted to say that this party stuff is genetic...

taken from the san francisco voters guide...

"B.Y.O.B" (Bring Your Own Ballot)

     There's an election coming up soon, so it must be PARTY TIME! PAUL 
KAMENY [yup that is my DAD!], a San Franciscan voter wrote and suggested 
that voters organize "Sample Ballot Parties."  I have heard about such 
gatherings for years and when Mr. Kameny came up with the suggestion of 
promoting these ballot parties throughout the city, I thought it was a 
great idea.  The party is an opportunity for everyone to learn about 
issues and/or candidates.  

1.  People invited to the party may be assigned a candidate or ballot 
measure to "become the expert on that subject."
2.  Each person brings there state and city voter information 
pamphlet/sample ballot to a gathering spot-someone's home, a neighborhodd 
church, a community center, or any place you name.
3.  While you eat, drink and socialize, either pot luck or compliments of 
the host, a moderator is chosen and everyone takes turns leading the 
discussion on a candidate or measure.
4.  The party may be nonpartisan or partisan, depending on the people you 
invite.
5.  Some parties only cover ballot measures, others concentrate on 
candidates, but many review both candidates and measures.
6.  No one needs to disclose how they will vote.

    I hope some of you organize "Sample Ballot Parties."  Let us know if 
you find your party as informative and fun as it has been for others who 
have attened past parties.  

     Your vote counts only if you cast your ballot,

                                           Germaine Q Wong
                                           Registrar of Voters

Actually my dad wrote a better blurb than this one but that is the jist 
of the idea...and don't forget to vote on june 7th.....
partyon...susie (:

Japan really isn't good at "one offs" in large warehouse type spaces because
all spaces are in use 24 hours per day.

Osaka is the hippest city with the widest underground dance scene however
Tokyo has the Cave- which has at least one night per week where trance
djs spin till dawn. The Cave club is in Shibuya district across from the
Bunkamura hall- at the top of the hill of the shops bordering on the 
hotel area. Most club listings have the Caves address.

Also check out the San Ni Pa club at 328 Roppongi Dori near Roppongi-
get off the Hibiya line at Roppongi Station, walk from the Almond landmark
store past the Wave record store and keep going- at 328 is a set of stairs
going downwards. Also in this district is club Yellow which has good
dance music.

Check out TKO Tokyo Knockout magazine for more listings of clubs

Well, I finally made it to an event in Portland that satisfied me
pretty thoroughly.  Natural High was held at the Roseland Theater,
which used to be a holy-roller temple until the early 1980s (it had
a 'Jesus Light of the World' sign on top of it like Gene Scott's
Church of the Open Door in LA), then it was Starry Night for a long
time (because of the previous management we used to call it the
Scary Fright).  Mostly it's a place for local metal and 'rock' bands
and touring groups of all kinds.  The last thing I saw there, in fact,
was Ken Kesey's traveling 'Twister' roadshow about ten days ago.  I've
seen all kinds of bands there over the years, from King Sunny Ade to
Gang of Four to Graham Parker to Fishbone.  Never thought of it as a
potential 'rave' site although it's apparently been the location for
a couple of parties in the past.  Anyway, it was quite an interesting
contrast!  

The Roseland is the upstairs part of a two-storey building downtown,
about six blocks from my office.  It's got a square shape inside, with
a big dance area and a balcony that wraps around on three sides, with
the stage on the fourth.  The sound system was basically the house's,
and it took a while for the sound guys to figure out how to EQ the
place for this kind of music, but when they did it was GOOD, though Buck
had to suffer through the worst of it and told me it sounded 'boomy'
up on stage where the mixer was.  I think this would be the KILLER place
for great sound if they could set up a quad, and I said as much to the
sound crew.  

I arrived right before 2 and unfortunately caught just the end of Taylor
playing, which is too bad because I've never heard his stuff and thought
he would be playing later.

Buck set up using a reel-to-reel deck (like at Launch Pad) but used it
only sparingly.  When you're set up on a stage things bounce, and in
this case the needles were noticeably bouncey whenever anyone stepped
on one of the loose boards.  I thought the second half of Buck's set
was really top notch.  Spun came on and did the *best* I've ever heard
him do -- his techniques are greatly improved from months ago (he's
always had great records).  I was out kickin' the dust on the dance
floor most of the night, which is not all that common for me.  The
message from the turntables was 'SF Funk, loud and clear' for both
Buck and Spun's sets.  Really good stuff.  Local DJ Mike Stevens 
followed with a very fine trance-y set, closing with the Delta Lady
track 'Anything You Want' which is a favorite.  Pasta finished off
with a good trance/house mixture.

I continue to be amazed at the skill and variety shown by the DJs 
on the west coast.  While we stick to our lower BPMs, there was a wide
range of music covered and it was well done all the way through.

The crowd was typical for Portland, very low key but not comatose, and
even a little vibey near the end which was kind of neat.  I think
attendance peaked around 400, and at least 100 were around at the end
around 7:30 (another unusual thing for Portland, where events often
shut down at 4:30 am as recently as last fall).

I did see Jess but didn't find you Vancouverites!  Sorry about that.
I was wearing my set of tags for the first time in quite a while,
complete with the nw-raves one.

After last year's optimistic start to summer with the awesome Get Down
Get Down Get Down Get Wicked at the Sonoma fairgrounds on Memorial Day,
things really went downhill for a while.  But I'm more hopeful about
this summer, not the least because a *really good* event was held within
walking distance (for a change!).

see you in the future

phred


~e

----- Begin Included Message -----


Hello folks.  An interesting peroject has come my way that I believe is of
interest to all Bay Area Internet folks - both experienced and curious.

A new resteraunt has opened in San Francisco, on the con\rner of 9th Street
and Folsom (where the Limbo and Billboard used to be).  This resteraunt, the
"ICON Byte Bar & Grill" is run by Joegh Bullock and Marcia Crosby, the main
folks behind the Climate Theatre.

When Marcia & Joegh came to me with the idea for this resteraunt a few months
ago, they described wanting to have a place that had a strong techno/cyber
feel to it and also *very comfortable* - a warm friendly place to eat really
good food, not a spiked-chrome-the-future-hurts place.

And they wanted to have Full Internet Access  in the resteraunt.

Well, months later and many strange events have pased, but it is a done deal
now and the place is open.

We have installed a dedicated Internmet connection (low speed -14.4K, but hey
it's a start :-) and a Macintosh running Mosaic etc.  This is all at a table
in the middle of the resteraunt and is available to customers to use.  At some
point there may be a rental fee for the keyboard, (like you leave your drivers
licsense at the bar and pay $6/hr or something) but at present it is part of
the meal :-)

I'm asking netheads and other curious people to come by and play with it - and
leave feedback.  There will be a notebook at the table to write stuff down,
and/or you can send me e-mail. (The resteraunt will have e-mail very soon:
icon@bytebar.com)

We have NCSA Telnet running so you can telnet anywhere in the world.

Sometimes the video gets routed to a video projector, so whatever you are doing
will be on the wall, 5 feet wide.

I'm working on a VERY BASIC and VERY READABLE cheat-sheet that wll be
laminated and hung by the table, saying things like "Please be patient - if
the little thing is spinning, don't click all over the place :-)".

We are building a home page that has pointers to cool stuff and we have a very
interesting "hotlist" installed.

And the food is really really good.

This is a interesting new opportunity to bring network communications into
everyday life, a little bit further.

So, y'all come by now.


ICON Byte Bar & Grill
299 9th Street (at Folsom)
San Francisco
 (in a week or so:  icon@bytebar.com   need time for the MX records to filter
out)

Subject: Followup on police crackdown on south of market clubs...
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

The Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control reports that surprise
joint weekend inspections with San Francisco police at 12 South of
Market night clubs have resulted in numerous citations of club owners.

According to ABC Director Jay Stroh, on several occasions near riots
have broken out, forcing police to call in tactical teams to disperse
crowds. On May 7, a disturbance at the Sound Factory at 525 Harrison
St. took police 2 1/2 hours to quell.

In a statement, Stroh called the situation ``out of control,'' adding
that it is impossible to prevent these clubs from serving alcohol to
minors or control the use of illegal drugs and the overcrowding that
sets the stage for a potential catastrophe.

On Friday and Saturday nights, ABC and San Francisco police visited
the Sound Factory, the Oasis, DV8, De Ja Vu, City Limits, 1015 Club,
Club Q, Pioneer, Paradise, City Nights, DNA and the Holy Cow.

A total of 28 arrests were made for violations involving minors in
public premises, minors drinking alcohol, public drunkeness, marijuana
possession, possession of a concealed weapon, resisting arrest and
assault on a peace officer.

Like the illegal ``rave'' clubs of Southern California, the South of
Market clubs charge entry fees and pack as many patrons inside as
possible, the statement said.

The clubs' setup makes enforcement or undercover operation difficult,
ABC reports, because of sophisticated security systems, with personnel
equipped with two-way radios and headphones.  Some clubs use metal
detectors.

On several occasions, ABC investigators trying to conduct a ``walk
through'' at a club were stalled by security personnel asking repeated
questions about the investigator's identity and purpose.
Investigators believe this was a delaying tactic while security guards
talked to those inside by radio, allowing them conceal anything
illegal, according to ABC.

[I believe here the police are more of a problem than the clubs ever
were. Reminds me of the recent Oakland "riot" which wasn't a riot
until the police showed up and started throwing their weight around.
Oakland police Capt. Michael Myers said ``later in the evening the
regular family people leave and you get the thugs showing up around 4
p.m.''  Call your representative and tell them your vote will go for
the candidate that works for real positive change and not one who
supports policemen who view people as "thugs". -Sean]

Subject: Sunset Sunday- (W)-ick (ed)-Long 
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Hay Ya!!!!

I went to Wicked, and although it was disappointing in many respects, i.e.,
the sound system,  little or no lighting or visual effects,  no bar (because
of the 18 over crowd)   I,  nevertheless,  managed to have another great
magical time.

 It seemed  that many of the Wicked regulars stayed away. I don't know if
they didn't wish to mingle with the teeners or what,  but the core Wicked
group, and the vibe they generate was't there.  Maybe they didn't want to get
coodies.

It's interesting that relativity is an absolute. By that I mean,
you don't know how good something was until it gets bad. No, I'm not talking
about love affairs, I'm talking about the sound system.

Rumor had it that the Wicked Posse didn't check the sound system before they
fired it up. That Jeno wanted to stop the music and put in a another mixer. I
imagine that would have been too much of a breach of rave protocal, anyway
the sound wasn't very alive. Highs and lows sounded homogenized, or a
 critical view would be it lacked crisp, clear definition, or
in other words, IT SUCKED.  "There's no place like Townsend, There's no place
like Townsend." Just click you heels together
and keep chanting that. But, to all the people I danced with and around, rox,
kenneth p. kristine, & teddy, you saved the evening!! Oh!! Thomas did stop
the music at 6:30 and kicked out the last set. Thomas; the anchor man, the go
to guy, closing another one out. Thanks, and kudos to him.

I talked to Preston a little, and bemoaned the loss of Light N Up. Now where
was I going to spend my hard earned after party dollars?

I was fortunate that Teddy and Kristine suggested the Sunset party at the
Berkeley Marina. Just the view across the bay was enough to get you off. I
understand they used to have they speakers turned north, so the wind would
blow the needle around, and blow the sound back toward the water.

Turning them up at the hill was the ticket. It was a beautiful day, and that
mellow summer vibe was starting to creep out of people's pores. The smell of
some roasting burgers or weenies would have done it.  Janie was bouncey and
bubbly enough to conjure up the summer spirits.

Thanks to John Howard for the nice outdoors set. It was fun dancing with
friends, and being able to see them.

We left about 8:00ish, but before we left everybody seemed to get the same
idea, to go to the top of the hill, and dancing together in the "remains of
the day." I looked like the closing scenes of Ingmar Bergman's SEVENTH SEAL,
where all the medieval peasants and serfs are dancing along the fortress
walls as blackened silhouettes. What a sight!!!

So, I give the Wicked party a 5 out of 10, and hope it serves as a
professional wake up call to the posse. No flame, just it's easy to become
complacent, and fly by the proverbial seat of your nickers.  Somebody told me
they were going to stop going to Martin's parties because they were dark and
beginning to feel depressing. I guess it begs the question: "Whose party is
it anyway?" The promoter's or the party goers? I thinks it's how parties can
begin to lose their center, and begin to fall apart.

Definite thumbs up to Sunset and the Sunday Dj's. Let's make it better by
having more people show up, and doing some serious outdoor trance dancing.
 (don't forget to bring goodies) Thanks SF.

Robert Johnson...Monterey

warm, cozy feel in the club. In Townsend, you say? Indeed. Dave of

colorful separation of the club. The sound system sounded GREAT  - kudos 
to John and Michael Krische,the latter of Terminator fame. DJ's are Pete 
Avila, Neon Leon, Swing Kid, Aaron O., and Jan Cooley. Dave had belly 
dancers on the platforms, which I thought was rather fun. According to my 
friends who investigated the dance floor, it had a great mix of fun, 
looking-good men and women. Townsend is 21+, but didn't seem to be 
targeted by Frank's gang of thugs. We'd love your support, so come down,

Cc: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject:  Re: more than just placards -Reply
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

	At a couple of events we've done here in Salt Lake City, we've had
couches and other chair-like things (beanbags, etc.) by the side of
the main dance area, but we found that it didn't work out very well. 
The reason why is because people will all be dancing, then some will
get tired and sit down, and those people sitting down will sort of
mentally drain the energy from the people still dancing.  I don't
know exactly how this happens, but it seems that it isn't as easy to
dance all night in front of people that are watching you like an
audience.  If everyone is grooving together, it's much better, but
when the crowd is split and half are sitting down and half are
dancing it doesn't work out.  Just my 2 cents.

Luke

	The song you're talking about is the classic (1992, that's old for
us young'uns...:) "Papau New Guinea" by the Future Sound of London. 
As for other Dead can Dance samplers, I've heard one ambient song
that sampled an entire 2 bar phrase from Dead can Dance and looped it
over and over to a simple drum-beat.  I can't recall the name of the
song, but this is a classic example of a Vanilla-Lice rip-off artist
in action.  Anyone can make good techno or house music if they steal
it from someone else... Papau New Guinea is a great song because they
simply took bits and pieces of a vocal sample and rearranged them in
a unique and creative way.
	While we're on the topic of Future Sound of London, be sure to keep
an eye out for their new album "LifeForms".  2 CD album for the price
of 1!  If you're into ambient music, this stuff will rock your
world... (yeah! rock on dude!!! :)

Luke

	This a bit from an e-mail letter I sent a friend...
	Please excuse the bit of hyperbole ;-)

        Forgot to tell you about the most amazing, stupendous,
        horrendous event we went to Sat. before last.  Yes, it was
        A CALCULATED FORCAST OF ULTIMATE DOOM!  Sickening Episodes
        of Widespread Devastation Accompanied by Sensations of
        Pleasurable Excitement.  In other words, a Survival Research
        Labs event!  It WAS truly amazing!  It was held in this abandoned
        steel fabricating building about 500 feet long and 80 feet wide
        and 60 feet high.  These nuts had built about 30 machines, some
        as big as bulldozers with huge metal grippers, spikes, rippers
        etc.  They built sonic cannon things that made huge concussions
        and screaming engine sounds SO LOUD it sounded like your head
        was stuck in a jet engine!  There was this one machine that looked
        like a huge jet engine that shot out flame about 6 feet in diameter
        in a HUGE blast.  It and all the other machines were under remote
        control and moved around on the concrete floor.  The flame cannon
        machine they had aimed against the back wall and it shot a jet
        of flame about 20 feet which hit the wall and spread out into
        a huge disk of flame about 20 feet in diameter.  At one point
        there was so much smoke inside the building and the heat from
        the flames so intense that people ran out the building to
        avoid getting their hair singed!  I can't tell you everyting
        they did but it was insane.  Barb wouldn't stay in there as
        she was too afraid of the one of machines going out of control
        and blasting the audience.  From outside (we could see in through
        huge open doors on the side of the building) we would hear blasts
        that were SO LOUD I couldn't believe the people inside could stand
        it!  In other words, IT WAS TOTALLY EXCELLENT!!!!  PS: they
        also had a huge clown head about 15 ft in diameter from the
        outside of a old amusement park that they had rigged on cables so
        they could move it up and down inside the building while huge
        machines torched it and whacked at it!  Now THAT'S ENTERTAINMENT!

        Enuff for now!  See yah!

        jamescotthompson - CUBE ROOT MOON BASE

Well after last weekend's SFPD and the ABC's action against SOMA, I've been
talking to some informed folks, (club managers etc.) about the ultimate goal of 
such action and most feel it's a prelude to a request by both agencies that 
afterhour action be ended in San Francisco. SF is one of the few cities in
the country
that allow people to stay in clubs past 2am. There have been several
comments by 
the ABC official in the press about how the clubs can't control drug use and 
afterhour drinking in the clubs, and the SFPD Southern station Liet. Hallisy 
is quoted in the Independent saying "It's a place for gangs to cruise and kids
from out of town to come and stay up all night. Booze, drugs, and being out all
night add up to violence."  There's a good chance this propaganda is
leading up to 
action to shutdown clubs at 2:00 am. 

Bob Hughes

Bob Hughes says:

>SF is one of the few cities in
>the country
>that allow people to stay in clubs past 2am. 

When I was living in Austin, TX, clubs would stay open all night.  They'd
be required to close the bar during certain hours, but the premesis would 
stay open and the DJs would keep playing dance music all night . . . people 
would stay around until noon the next day.

In Chicago, I've gone to clubs that had live bands, and the headliners
wouldn't even come on until about 2am or so (to be specific, I'm 
thinking of a Pop Will Eat Itself show at the Caberet Metro).

New York City clubs close at 4am, not 2am.  They've had after-hours
problems lately, too, though.  It's funny that the NYC and SF after-hours
problems have "cropped up" at the same time that house/rave culture has
left the warehouses and moved into the clubs.

>the ABC official in the press about how the clubs can't control drug use and 
>afterhour drinking in the clubs, 

They can control afterhour drinking by totally closing the bar down 100%,
and having the last call being at like 1:15 or 1:30 if the drinking needs
to be over and done with by 2:00 am.  That's what they did in Austin.  If 
there is no way for people in the club to get the booze after hours, then 
there is no way there can be after-hours drinking then, eh?

As for the drug problem . . . I find it amusing that during the big
cocaine days of the 80's nightlife and clublife-all-night flourished,
but now that people are doing other things the police in places like
New York and San Francisco are getting all worried.  Back in the 80's
when doctors and lawyers were doing coke in clubs no one really cared,
but now that "crufty raver types" are taking those "nasty psychedelics"
then "it must be stopped."

Two-faced law-enforcement agencies.  Bah.

Laura

>Remember these all happened in SOMA nightclubs, not raves.  The cops are

Agreed.  In fact, I would love it if the cops would come by and check out
parties every now and then, if they do it right.  In the same vein, I
feel better for some reason when the cops come to a renegade party, 
check it out, and leave, than if they never come at all.  A good example
was witnessed Sat. night at Wicked - there were a couple cops (both
uniformed and plainclothes) outside the door that night, just making sure
things were cool while people were waiting in line, but they weren't 
doing anything intrusive at all.  In fact one cop was seen laughing 
for minutes after he was hugged by a girl out of the blue, setting off his 
radio transceiver.

However, the flip side of the coin is that police cheifs and politicians
aren't interested in distinguishing between "good parties" and "bad
parties".  As we've seen, they consider all organized activity after
2am to be a contributing factor to violence and disorderliness.  This
is the problem.

        Brian

Miles' address is in the UK.  I don't know if you're aware of what
events are going on over there right now, but the government is
attempting to make it illegal for any group of people to gather if
they are throwing a "rave", or planning a "rave."  With all the
negative publicity that's been spoon-fed to the American public by
the government-controlled media in our country, I could easily see
the same type of law being passed over here in a few years.  There's
no way that our house/rave community is big enough for us to just say
"ravers unite and start a revolution," but in the UK, it possibly is.
Just because you live in SF doesn't mean you're in the center of the
world's cultural community.  Almost every aspect of rave culture that
is dominant in America came from the UK, and we have a lot to learn
from their successes and failures.
	Hearing someone else's opinion, no matter how stupid, isn't going to
hurt you one bit, and it might actually help you.  Why don't we
espouse a little more of the values we claim to, rather than jumping
down somebody else's throat whenever they say something out of the
ordinary.  I don't mean to be rude to you personally, Brian, it just
bothers me when people get flamed for no reason.  They might actually
have something good to say, but after being flamed once or twice like
that, who knows if they'll ever post again?

Peace,
Luke

On Wed, 8 Jun 1994, Laura La Gassa wrote:

> They can control afterhour drinking by totally closing the bar down 100%,
> and having the last call being at like 1:15 or 1:30 if the drinking needs
> to be over and done with by 2:00 am.  That's what they did in Austin.  If 
> there is no way for people in the club to get the booze after hours, then 
> there is no way there can be after-hours drinking then, eh?
> 
Two of my ex-roommates were bartenders for DV8, Crazy Eights and 
Sound Factory (free booze *chuckle*) and once two am hit, they and the 
other staff would always go around pulling cups right out of people's 
hands. Rude, yes, but noone I knew at any of the 'publicly-accessible' 
clubs would have been crazy enough to risk their jobs and substantial 
fines by selling alcohol after 2. The catch is: its not illegal to DRINK 
alcohol in a bar after 2 a.m. It's only illegal to SELL it after 2 a.m. 
The cops instantly assume any alcohol in a club was sold by the club and 
thus have the meat for a trumped-up sweep of every SOMA bar listed in the 
Guardian.

This action is total crap as they obviously plan to do nothing else but 
harrass people and make the pissed-off element even more pissed-off. When 
that anger turns violent, as it always does, they're conveniently 
elsewhere (usually busily writing parking tickets). The bigger clubs here 
are crime-ridden (I've got an inch-long scar under my eye thanks to 
SoundFactory), but this little show-of-force is only going to make it 
worse in the long run.

There's obviously an ulterior motive involved...

> 	often their presence is in semi-riot gear.  they seem to
> 	not mention this happening weekly, culminating in a non-
> 	injury shooting a few weeks ago, in their attacks on the
> 	after hours 'problem.'  i wonder why?

Because it blows away their theory that shutting everyone down at 2 will
solve the non-existent 'problem'.

Crime is, by definition, a conflict.  Police rampaging through a club
of happy party people creates conflict, and some percentage of that
may very well be crime.  "See?  People are doing bad stuff!  We've got
to stop it!"  Well, had you not goaded them, they might have gone on
happily partying, but now they're fearful and pissed off, and will react
badly.

Most crime can be traced back to the _imposition_ of law.  If we make more 
crimes, we make more criminals.  What proportion of these busts are for 
victimless crimes like drug (including alcohol) use, and what proportion
are for actual violation of another's rights?

This, Brian U., is why I'm an anarchist, but only as a byproduct of my
other beliefs.  I take responsibility for myself -- I do not expect
anyone else to rescue me from my stupidity -- but I enjoy the fruits
of free action -- I do not expect anyone else to stand in my way.
Well, there are many organizations around right now whose sole purpose
is to coerce your behavior by threat of force; they're called
governments, and have no other function.  I try to live up to my
responsibility, and am trying to find modes of life that do not depend
on these institutions that oppress us.  If you have a big
agglomeration of millions of people like SF that cannot support itself
(must import its food and export its waste), and that people must compete with
each other merely to get a roof over their heads, _of course_ you need
police, governments, big corporations, and other dominance-hierarchy
based organizations to keep it from disintegrating!
	If we don't change ourselves first, any revolution will be just that:
a full circle which returns us to our starting place.

Rant off.

// g

As a followup to my short post yesterday, which, admittedly I fired off a
little hastily ( State oppression....) I ought to explain what's happening
in the UK.

At the end of last year our beloved Home Secretary announced that his
government would be launching a full-scale crakdown on "Ravers, Squatters and
travellers"

The Criminal Justice Bill now making its' way through parliament and due to
become law contains some of the following.....

- Clauses 47-50 make it a criminal offence to hold a party or rave without a
  licence (punishable by a prison sentence and/or 2500 pound fine).

- If a police officer 'believes' ten or more people are gathered making
  preparations for a rave or merely waiting for one to start the police can
  declare an exclusion zone of a mile in radius. Anyone remaining in the zone
  can face arrest and be punished by a prison sentence and/or 2500 pound fine

- Clause 61 removes the duty of local authorities to provide sites for
  travellers. (i.e. the homeless).

- Clauses 56-57 makes a squatter or homeless person a criminal if they do not
  leave their temporary home within 24 hrs of being served a possession order.

- Clause 54 makes it an offence for more than 20 people to gather on land of
  what the police believe to be of'historical, architectural or archaeological
  importance'.

- Clauses 52-53 make a new offence of criminal trespass which would make
  criminals of people demonstrating against the destruction of our environment
  such as obstructing a truck or digger. Punishable by prison sentence and/or
  2500 pound fine.


Part of the Crininal Justice Bill attempts to define dance music and to outlaw
the playing of it in the open air. It's definition.....

"SOUNDS WHOLLY OR PREDOMINANTLY CHARACTERISED BY THE EMISSION OF A
SUCCESSION OF REPETITIVE BEATS"

The police and government of the UK are determined that there will be NO MORE
raves in our country.

The last 'legal' raves here last year cost the organisers ten thousand pounds
for the licence and fortyfive thousand pounds for the police bill.


I'm not a violent person, but this sort of legislation makes peaceful people
fucking angry!


Miles

"violence at clubs" which means that they're going into South of 
Market clubs and looking anything they find illegal... so be careful
and be peaceful.

From: child@netcom.com (Spaced-Out Funky Earthchild)
Message-Id: <199406092150.OAA21629@netcom.com>
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
In-Reply-To: Don Labutay's message of Wed, 8 Jun 94 7:51:44 PDT <9406081452.AA22257@vestek.com>
Subject: Followup on police crackdown on south of market clubs...
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU


>I support what the cops are doing right now with the SOMA clubs. 
>I have seen the violence in these clubs and it should be stop. Here are
>some of the incidents that I saw:   
<various incidents of bodily violence recounted here>

Well, I for one, do not wish to live in a situation where there are police
everywhere looking at everything you do to see if you've done something that
someone has written a law against (eg. it's illegal to pump your own gas in
Oregon). 

I personally do not think that cops are out there to protect you.  The only
way all these fights could be prevented is to have a cop everywhere all the
time.  Through my perception, cops are not out there to keep you from getting
hurt - they are here to ENFORCE the law.  There is a huge difference.  

In my opinion, when cops go and bust a lot of clubs to make splashy news, they
did it because their sergeant told them to.  And their sergeant told them to
because in some meeting with the sergeants, the commanding officer said, "let's
hit the clubs ... that's the word from the chief"  And the chief told them to
bust the clubs because he wants to further his career and the careers of his
superiors who want to show the public that, "You see, I'm doing something about
crime!"  Thus high profile club busts is politically motivated, in my 
opinion.  I mean it was the weekend before the local voting took place.
You can call that corruption or you can call it the way the system is
running these days or you can call it silly or you can disagree with me.

I believe that the ultimate responsibility for one's physical or mental safety
should rest with oneself.  You can lazily delegate it to a force which is 
quickly gaining more and more power in the last 2 decades and hope that they
don't overstep your bounds someday.  But for my sake puuhleeeeseee don't do 
that in the same town that I'm in cuz I'm for personal freedom.  Until a person
has a weapon such as a gun, s/he has only as much power as you allow him/her.
Note that all cops wear guns.  That's far too much already, in my opinion.

Don, if you don't want to witness all this violence, then I suggest you visit
other more peaceful house venues of which there are many.  Stay away from a
crowd sporting a macho vibe and I noticed that most of the venues you listed
are at places that have a large section of clientelle suscribing to the 
macho 'tude.  I personally haven't seen much violence this
year at all, I've seen a total of maybe 4 fights so far and I happened to be
right there in between the two contestants at one Bonny Doon fight and I kept
them apart and their fighting energy was dissipated. 

At Sunday's Spundaes on memorial day weekend, I saw a fight (one of the guys
seemed to be looking for anybody to fight with and he got a taker) and 
many people kinda stopped dancing and started rubbernecking.  My question was:
if 2 people are going to fight, why give them so much energy by giving them
your attention units?  I mean, there's also babies being born in the local
hospital, there's people are giving eachother love over there, there's so 
much other stuff to give your attention units to.

Here's my motto on violence:
Do not hate or fear violence - you will only bring it towards you, in a 
round-about "coincidental" fashion that fear and hate tend to do.   Instead, 
love peace.  

There are many subtle shades of delicate paranoia - don't get caught up with
them, unless you want to, of course.


Love, peace, acceptance, unity, forgiveness,

Spaced-out Funky Earthchild

Coupla comments-

At 10:53 AM 06/09/94 -0700, David Alves wrote:

>The most reasonable idea I have heard was the "set the tone for summer"
>explanation - where the police are making themselves very visible 
>right now.

Election year. Tough on crime. War on drugs. Three strikes. SFPD.
I think it all makes a lot of sense.

>Doesn't it make sense that the best use of their time would be a
>coordinated (abc/cops) *highly* visible short term effort to make it
>seem like a bad place for committing crimes.  It would be like
>the sobriety check points which are 100% P.R. 

sobriety check points also serve to catch a lot of outstanding warrants
and minor infractions for tickets. Captive audience...and money is money.
The use of sobriety check points is, at least to legal theorists, on
shakey constitutional ground, and one of the few places the police can
use a guilty until proven innocent approach, and the milk it.

-j

You are right- after looking at my last message I realized
I made only a little sense. "But what I meant to say was"

There was a court decision somewhere (forget the specifics)
that established the police right to require one to stop to
prove sobriety to move from point a to point be via a specific
route, where they can't in (most) other situations. This was
decided based on the percieved risk of drunk driving overriding
consitiutional right. And they use it for all sorts of things
that don't have a whole lot to do with alcohol.

Wendy reminded me that I forgot something important (what isn't)
in my Why I Wasn't at IN THE LIGHT (EarthSpace Seattle) post last
week.

How many times has this happened to/with you/yours?

When the music was cut at 3:45 or whatever, people kept dancing!
One man (Ferdous) had a drum - the only one!(?)  Lots of people
clapped - I mean clapped together - nice patterns 'n' stuff, y'know?
Trying and succeeding to keep "it" going.  Then a couple of people
started chanting.  It went on for a nice long time and darn it, it
was sweet!

I remember this phenomena at the end of the Marx Meadow dances those
long two summers ago.  And at the end of Boggie Buffet sometimes.

I think we're on to something here. (something old, something new...)

Oh yeah, so Ferdous stopped drumming a couple of times, and you could 
feel the vacuum just like when the sound cuts out.  I think he did, 
too, because he would start again and you could just feel this "Whew!
It's still going" uh... something  in the... ayer

 Grey Six's post about live drummers reminds me of a similar incident
at a Richmond Civic event ( a "last" Gathering? ). At the end , after the
music was cut off , a guy continued to drum on an overturned plastic
drum - he was good too! They asked him to stop so that Martin could
be heard saying his thanks - yous .

 MOTION in San Jose has occasionally had live percussionists - the promoter
just asks them to play someplace away from the DJ , in order not to be a
distraction during the mixing. I've had the best dance/trancing at MOTION 
by dancing near the drummers and the speakers.

I believe a breakbeat is something that has syncopation in it--ie, a beat that 
doesn't conform directly to the meter.  Jeno's "Energy" and Garth's "Break It
Down" both have songs with 'breakbeat' in them.  

As far as "progressive house" goes, who knows?  I thought it was all 
"progressive".

I'm sure others have different definitions, but my sense of 'breakbeat'
as a style is fairly fast (140-160 bpm) stripped-down tracks with drums,
bass and very little other instrumentation.  The amount of syncopation
varies a lot.  I almost never hear breakbeat played in SF and the Northwest.

'Progressive house' is a vague catch-all category for a style of house
that is less vocal-dependent or takes a more 'alternative' production
approach to the track than the usual club-style house.  Many people in
the east think that 'progressive house' is all that gets played on the
west coast, though that's hardly true.  The dividing line between
'progressive house' and what some call 'deep house' is more a matter of
gradient than kind.  I wonder what other people here would consider to
be representative tracks of 'progressive' and 'deep' house.  I suppose
the Sasha remix of 'Talk To Me' is progressive . . .
