From: anthrax@uclink.berkeley.edu (Ann Elizabeth Loraine)
Message-Id: <199406112207.PAA02632@uclink.berkeley.edu>
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: a very long New Moon review
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

A Very Long New Moon Reveiw  

Well, I should say first off that since I'm part of the group that put
this on, I'm a little biased...but I wanted to post on it so you all
know how it went and might get influenced to go to the next one!  Which
may be at the end of June at Gregg's house.  It's not the new moon then,
but we want to have a going-away party for Glen and Heather.  

The crew, et. al. assembled at Heather & Glen's apt on Stanyon St.
beginning around 2 pm.  We were hoping to be on the road by 3, but you
know how that goes!  Since the party was also supposed to be Glen and
Heather's wedding, it took a lot more preparation than usual, but it
turned out to definitely be worth it in the end.  

Heather and Glen were busily making last-minute calls and wrapping
presents when we got there.  Has anyone out there been in a wedding? 
You know how stressful it is!  The bride and the groom are always
stressed (a little to a lot) and the others invovled pick up on that and
get stressed because it's supposed to be a SPECIAL DAY, you know, the
day the married couple remember for the rest of their lives, and this
knowledge somehow makes it harder.  But Heather and Glen were holding it
together incredibly well...they have been living together for many years
and they have the couple thing down now, no problem.  They've also
organized several parties besides this one and know exactly what to do
and when to do it.

After arranging the rides for people, the generator, the sound system,
the presents, the altar, etc., we finally got on the road about 4:30. 
The party was to be held at Goat Rock, which is out by Bodega Bay.  A
word on the location:  it's beauty is astonishing, and worth the drive. 
I would say this would even be a good spot for the FMR at some point,
but I want to give a word of caution:  the tides there are very
treacherous.  The ranger gave us a very solemn warning:  several people
die there every year.  Also, the tide comes in pretty far in some
places, and if you don't know the site, you might be tempted to set up
on a beach that will pretty much vanish during high tide.  When the tide
comes in, you have to climb over rocks if you want to get to the one
safe spot about 1/2 mile down the beach.  At one point in the evening,
we set up a string of candles to guide late-comers.  Gregg led a group
of already slightly drunk kids over the bad part around midnight, and
they were having some trouble.  Once again, this confirmed for me the
dangers of alcohol.  How I wish wish wish that pot (and other things)
were decriminalized.  *sigh*  Finally:  use of this site requires a good
dose of responsibility on the part of the organizers to make sure those
with altered judgement and motor skills make it through the night.

The site of the party was a cove maybe 1/2 to 3/4 miles from the parking
lot.  Much thanks goes out to those who helped haul everything that far.
 (If you read this, thanks thanks thanks, Lain & Phillip, two Sfravers
that helped out big time! You helped set up and helped break it
down..you are the coolest!)

On the system:  Galen brought Pacific Sound, his new
soundsystem.  Everyone there commented again and again on how good it
sounded.  It's been getting a lot of use lately:  last weekend he took
it to the Hemp Expo and played an awesome set there and the next day he
did his Sunset party with djs Dante & Buck.  And this Friday he did
another set with it at Ananda, despite being dead tired I expect from
the New Moon party.  

Everything was all set up a little bit before sunset, and Charles
Alexander started us out with an increasingly more mellow ambient set as
the afternoon faded into night.  The altar was set up against the base of the
cliff..there were sunflowers plus the usual candles and other meaningful
objects.  The main piece, though, was a large print of the same image
(two children holding hands before a glorious sunset) that was on the
cover of the wedding invitation/flyer-for-the-party.  

Heather & Glen were to be married by Dave Washer (the surfer/clothes
designer/artist who suggested the site) and Mona Love, mother of the New
Moon party.  Our unofficial flower-girl was beautiful Jasmine (nicknamed
Jazzy, and only 2 anahaf) who spied the wedding cake before anyone else!
 The ceremony began after everyone assembled before the altar.  Dave
told us all a little about Heather and Glen and about all our roles in
the ceremony.  He said that we all, not just Mona and himself, were to
be the ones marrying them.  He said that the ceremony was to be about
healing, both ourselves and the planet.  He also said that love is
necessary for healing and that simply being present was an expression of
love.  We all joined hands and he instructed us to meditate on this
thought as Heather and Glen, in soft voices, exchanged their vows.  Then
he asked us all to pronounce them married.  The crowd all said, pretty
much in unison, "I now pronounce you man and wife!"  Then a little giggle
went around as many of the women, including myself, said "I now
pronounce you HUSBAND and wife." 

 Then Mona sent into the crowd a piece
of cord and asked everyone to tie a knot into it to symbolize the
binding ties of love.  When this had returned to the altar, Heather and
Glen stood up and told us all about how they first met and also what it
has meant to them to be part of this "rave community," which to them is
about collectivism and cooperation and love and healing.  They told us
all that they hoped to someday be part of such a community again, as they are
moving to Philadelphia soon so that Heather can attend medical school
there.  Then Dave laughed, saying that "you seem to attract this kind of
thing!"  And then Glen said he has never felt so much love from so many
people and will remember us always.

Then Dave announced that as part of the wedding ceremony, Heather and
Glen would be passing out pouches that Heather and a friend had made. 
Everyone was asked to find a stone or shell or some other object from
the beach to put in this pouch, which they hoped we would then place on
our own altars or other such place to keep forever to reminds us of
their wedding.  As another keepsake, they also gave each person a
fimo pendant containing a pattern of flowers and painted with the
symbols "G & H 1994."    

The ceremony ended when Morgan suggested that we all stand up, join
hands, and make a circle.  We did, and all were astonished to realize
how many of us there were...maybe 70 or so.  We all started whooping and
when it stopped, the wedding was over.

Then the party began.  The music was ambient until 2 or 3.  Ambient djs
were Graham, Nick Philips and Charles Alexander.  People settled in
around the fires, talked and got to know each other during this time.  A
couple of people were antzy..."when's the house going to start!?!" they
were asking.  But most agreed that some hours of ambient set the
mood...sort of like foreplay and thus are absolutely necessary to
achieve the perfect New Moon effect!

The first house/dance dj to start was the incomparable Scott Hardkiss. 
His set was the sleekest of house shot through with veins of funk &
hiphop.  The generator crapped out a couple of times..after one breakdown, he
put on a housed-up Stones song that people really dug.  He was
absolutely amazing.  Then Galen went on.  His set was straight-up house.
 Galen wins the Iron dj award..he spun for five ana half hours.  (No
wonder Ananda got off to a late start..sorry guys!) In the morning,
Dante took over with some incredible acid jazz.  It was worth the wait. 
Now I know that acid jazz is the thing for me!  Then Mark Farina spun. 
A couple of us danced it all the way through out in the surf, 'cause the
sand was burning our bare feet.  A few folks walking their dogs gave us
funny looks...I wonder what they thought!

Around 2 we started breaking it down.  The thirty or so people there
pitched in with the haulage of items back to the parking lot.  Thanks!
Thanks also  go out to Allen of Ameba and Michelle who transported the
sound system back to SF.  Thanks also go out to Rick Webb, who stayed
til the very end, hauled stuff and made sure the beach was as beautiful
when we left as when we arrived.

Whew!  What a party!

love,

annthrax

Subject: Re: Who's breakbeat?
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Breakbeat is a dance subgenre that is characterised by syncopated
hip-hop style beats -- in fact, many early breakbeat tracks contained
loops of sped-up hip-hop beats.  In 1991-1992 a lot of breakbeat 
featured sped-up vocals that sounded almost like Alvin and the
Chipmunks.

When they refer to "hardcore" in the UK, they mean what we call
"breakbeat."  "Jungle" is another term for breakbeat.

Most breakbeat is fairly fast by San Francisco standards -- 135
to 210 beats per minute.  The REALLY fast stuff, though, was only
popular for a short amount of time I think.

The only breakbeat DJ I know of in San Francisco is Demigod.  
He played at Apocalypse from time to time.  The slower funky
groovy syncopated stuff Jeno plays can also be thought of as breakbeat,
but the breakbeat DJs I know prefer to call it "that San Francisco
breaky stuff" or "trip-hop" due to its hip-hop style beats.

"Progressive House" is a sort of follow-on from house.  It 
really isn't clear why it is named this, but it's a more technoy
trancey form of house, with harder "fatter" beats and a bit faster
than other forms of house, and less use of vocal samples.  A lot
of what Lee An plays can be classified as progressive house (and
also as a few other things -- he has a good amount of variety of
styles in his sets :-) ).

Will can probably define prog. house better than me . . . if you
heard him at the Blue Cube or Launch Pad, a lot of what he played
are good examples of progressive house.

Laura

>Will can probably define prog. house better than me . . .

I think you did a pretty good job.  Let's see...

>it's a more technoy trancey form of house,

it's known by a number of people as just plain techno house if that makes
more sense to you.

>with harder "fatter" beats and a bit faster
>than other forms of house, and less use of vocal samples.

yes, yes, yes.
Progressive house in England is comparable to the amount of house that gets
played here.  Most of it comes from the UK while some from Belgium,
America, & Italy.  The more commercial variety (like Sasha) comes closer to
deep house as it has more wailing divas, pianos, etc. while the more
underground variety has no divas and borrows more from trance, tribal, &
acid but keeping with house beat.

some labels:  guerrilla, hard hands, soma, limbo

>I'm sure others have different definitions, but my sense of 'breakbeat'
>as a style is fairly fast (140-160 bpm) stripped-down tracks with drums,
>bass and very little other instrumentation.  The amount of syncopation
>varies a lot.  I almost never hear breakbeat played in SF and the
>Northwest.

Actually it now goes up to 170bpm (and I hear of faster tunes).
But "very little other instrumentation" is not at all accurate.  There
are vocal samples, acid synths, strings, etc.  I think what you say
might apply to "gabber".

>'Progressive house' is a vague catch-all category for a style of house
>that is less vocal-dependent or takes a more 'alternative' production
>approach to the track than the usual club-style house.  Many people in
>the east think that 'progressive house' is all that gets played on the
>west coast, though that's hardly true.  The dividing line between
>'progressive house' and what some call 'deep house' is more a matter of
>gradient than kind.  I wonder what other people here would consider to
>be representative tracks of 'progressive' and 'deep' house.  I suppose
>the Sasha remix of 'Talk To Me' is progressive . . .

This is a very "circular" description.  You are assuming that the
questioner, who does not know the "progressive house" term, nevertheless
understands what you mean hear by "alternative" or "deep house" for that
matter.  I've seen Steve Hillage and The Orb describe their 777 album as
"deep house", but I don't think they mean the same thing as you do. :-)

respect,

    Ken
    Ken.Stuart@tigerteam.org

From sfraves-owner  Mon Jun 13 02:26:03 1994
Received: by techno.Stanford.EDU (4.1/1.34)
	id AA22551; Mon, 13 Jun 94 02:26:03 PDT
Received: from well.sf.ca.us by techno (4.1/1.34)
	id AA22538; Mon, 13 Jun 94 02:25:51 PDT
Received: (from phred@localhost) by well.sf.ca.us (8.6.9/8.6.9) id CAA04466 for sfraves@techno.stanford.edu; Mon, 13 Jun 1994 02:26:25 -0700
Date: Mon, 13 Jun 1994 02:26:25 -0700
From: Fred Heutte <phred@well.sf.ca.us>
Message-Id: <199406130926.CAA04466@well.sf.ca.us>
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: Disappointment
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Finding myself in SF on a Saturday night, and not having been to a
'commercial' event in several months, I tossed a coin and went to
Fundamental last night.  It's the same place as the last Wicked,
a Latino cultural center at 2929 19th between Florida and Alabama,
only about six blocks from 16th & Harrison, actually (which had
Indonesia last night and was totally packed, all rooms being used,
according to what DRC told me today).

About the only good thing I can say for Fundamental is it wasn't too
crowded, thanks perhaps to the big turnout at the Haze.  Aside from
the usual lackadaisical and snotty door security, it was easy to get
into and the price ($10) seemed right.  Upstairs, a large rectangular
room and a smaller one, each with a sound system.  Jeno and Doc were
going toe to toe when I arrived (around the same time as Ethan, as it
turned out).

But the sound wasn't good in either room and to make things worse, Jeno
had it cranked up to the point of painful distortion (it got a little
better when Markie took over).  Doc was trying but had turntable problems
(more on that in a bit).  There was virtually no vibe to be found, 
except for Carlos, El Faro del Sur, who was flyering for his new Thursday
club.

Ethan left shortly thereafter, and no more than two minutes after he did
this woman (clubber type) who had come in the small room when Neon Leon
took over from Doc, comes over to me and demands to know, in the 
Immortal Four Words, . . .

"Are you a COP?!?!?"

I've told you all about my experiences with this line of inquiry in
my lovely but suspicion-ridden hometown, Portland.  She followed this
after my protestations to the contrary with, "Well, do you have any
drugs on you," and I realized this is now the two-part colloquy in a
certain part of the scene.  

All I can say is, it wasn't so long ago when this was a scene where you
were presumed to be what you acted like.  Since I was bopping along to
the ultra-hard house Leon was laying out, it looked like I was a devoted
if somewhat goofy looking out-of-towner, which I am.  But I am also a
scenester of some considerable experience.  And to me this little encounter
epitomizes what is going wrong with the big parties (or even medium sized
ones like this).  They have frozen into an unchanging pattern and allowed
a great deal of mischief and bad feelings and dealings to emerge.

Shortly after this I moved closer to the DJ setup.  Someone either bumped
the table or stepped on a board causing the needle to skip, right as Leon
was about to crossfade.  He immediately stepped back in disgust and
began motioning people away from the table.  I thought this was in good
fun, as Doc had grimaced but gracefully moved on when this happened a
couple of times, but instead Leon decided to pout.  He went to the
back corner for a minute or two before resuming.  The vibe in the room
just *sagged*.  Hissy fits from DJs may make for dramatic moments, but
this seemed a bit beyond.  Perhaps I misconstrued what happened, and
Leon has earned my respect as a DJ over and over again in the past for
his very perceptive selection and mixing techniques, but this just
aggravated what was rapidly becoming a downward trend.

Finally, in the big room, Jeno chose to finish up with the ugliest,
rawest stuff I've heard him play.  I'm not demanding that every cut
he or any other DJ play be in the happy-vibe category, but this just
seemed destined to bring out the adrenalin/testosterone response from
the crowd.  

Jeno and Doc at 4 am in a decent space and not too crowded, sounded like
a winning combo, right?

I left soon after Markie began his spinning.  He wasn't doing much better,
although at that point I'll admit my attitude was soured on the whole 
thing.

It seems petty to write all this up this way, but I'm simply trying to
reflect my honest response.  A kind of Gresham's Law syndrome has prevailed
over the commercial party scene in the last 18 months.  In thinking back
on it, the last truly memorable one I've been to in SF was a Funky Techno
Tribe at the Galleria where Tony just put us in orbit, and that was last
September as I recall . . .

The thing that impressed me most last night, after filtering out the
little incidents I mentioned here, was the absolute lack of good vibe
among the crowd.  It reminded me of the first time I went to NAF in
Seattle last summer, when only Donald Glaude spinning wake-up house
at 6 am outside managed to salvage a nearly worthless night.  

And yet, commercial events *can* go off, as an excellent one here in
Portland just last week proved.  

Having watched the Grateful Dead more or less disintegrate into a
pleasant but bland outfit just the previous night at Cal Expo in
Sacramento, it reminded me of what happened just two years ago when
I went directly from a Dead show at Cal Expo to an excellent Thursday
night affair at Townsend with Garth and others spinning, when it 
really was more for fun.  

And it still is fun overall -- I love my DJ practicing and record buying,
the small events this year have been great, and it's exciting to make
contact with folks both at home and around the world who are tuned into
this wave.  But it's sad to see a great if short-lived institution like
the SF rave massive turned into just another all-night warehousing of
atavistic citizens on the loose.

phred

I think that SF is in the hands of Big Business at the moment. I think 
they are pretty much calling the shots at this point.

The cops, IMHO, are trying to get rid of an element they can't control. 
Things like 'raves' are just by their very nature _not_ in their control, 
and man, they *really* hate that! They want everyone to be knocking their 
heads on the floor toadying up to them... case in point-- my stepmom used 
to manage the Keystone way back when, and they used to pay off the cops 
on a routine basis to keep from being harassed. This stuff with the SOMA 
clubs really makes their political agenda obvious.  Mayor Frank Jordan 
needs to be soundly *thrashed* for his knee-jerk right-wing actions. 
Like, we now have fingerprint scanning devices that we pay for to 
supposedly catch 'welfare cheaters'. That system has cost *alot* of 
money, and so far they've found 1 (ONE) person who was getting benefits 
illegally. Can you say "blame the victim? I know that you can..."

Also, there's that stupid "smoke a joint, lose your license" crap too. 
I've been writing/faxing our alleged representatives for weeks on that one.
I don't even know what's going on in The City at the moment; they managed 
to "lose" 10ks worth of absentee ballots, so I and many others just 
couldn't vote. Coincidence? I don't think so...

Enough for now... Gotta go...

Peace!

Maui

World Groove will be a huge party held at the Cow Palace, which is 
where they have professional basketball games, so it is BIG.  It
will have lots of bands, so it could be intersting in a concert
sense, but many people are doubtful of the vibe.

Back-to-Basics 2nd Year Anniversary will be a medium sized party, not
sure of the location.  The fact that one of you is only 17 might be
a problem, as sometimes there are 18+ age restrictions, you should
call the phone line or even email Martin himself to make sure if you
decide to go to this one.  The last Basics party I went to they did
check IDs.  Basics parties seem to be very consistent, so I'd pick
this over World Groove -- good DJs, good overall production, and a
good group of people usually attend.

I am biased (being one of the DJs), but I'm going to be at Friends and
Family.  Even if I weren't spinning I'd still be there.  It will be
a small party, I believe with no age restriction, and it's put on
by a big bunch of SFRaves people and that produces a family sort of
vibe.  The the music will be a mixture of the acid/trance/progressive/
experimental vein along with some more straight-up house.  Spun will 
be spinning, along with Alex from Gaia Mantra, the usual Liquid Air
DJs, and Tamotsu. There will be a seperate chill area with ambient 
all night long, featuring all net-DJs including Joe Rice from LA; there 
will be a special live performance by Weird Blinking LIghts and also a 
sort of guided visualization of quantum physics by Ovid with music spun
by M. Normal.  It will be cool.  And all this for only $3.  Finger
my account for the flyer.

From: nrg@netcom.com (ethan miller)
Subject: Re: Disappointment
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Sorry to pitch in on a negative tip but I feel even more strongly than fred
does about just how bad fundamental was not only as itself byt also as a
representative of commercial parties in general. I only stayed 20 minutes
but here are my observations:

Sound:
Like Wicked the sound systems *sucked*! While at least in this case they
"worked" they were overdriven at the amps and then to make it worse, by the
djs. My ears are still ringing.

Space:
This space is from hell. Call me oversensitive or whatever but this space
exudes a bad vibe. It's dark, it's cavernous, there's no ventilation. It
feels trapped in 1970. The installed tracklight spots of yellow and red
that both Wicked and fundamental used just feel totally cheesy. Adding *a*
blacklight just doesn't make the diffference. The smaller room is decidedly
better and, used by itself might be workable. Architecturally it's much
more interesting, acoustically much more promising, and generally just
*feels* better. But to put it in real perspective: the trocadero blows this
space away...

Vibe:
This is what really hurts. For the first time I was surrounded by people
who were obviously (and by their own admission) twisted. I certainly have
no objection to this but at fundamental I couldn't escape the perception
that I was surrounded by a huge illusion. There was no vibe anywhere yet
everybody was totally glazed jumping up and down ferociously, sweating,
their eye's bulging, drunkeness obvious in many cases. School is obviously
out and I shudder to think that the numerous absolute newbies I encountered
there went home thinking that this is what raving in SF is like...

Cost:
This is the only good thing I have to say about fundamental. As compared to
Wicked: fundamental delivered two rooms, twice the number of DJs,
drastically better visuals (Lon of PURE is a toal genius), actually did
something with the halls (instead of just leaving the flourescents on for
chrissake) for $5 *less*.

In sum:
If this is what the summer has to offer, then this scene at least as far it
relates to the "big" promoters is on its way down. And guess what: it's all
about *money*. The big promoters are using this space cos: it's big, it's
relatively cheap, it's got police protection, and it's all ages, ie. they
can count on making their money. I SAY SCREW THEM! They're ripping *you*
off, they're ripping *me* off and worst of all they're making this scene
look (and sound) like shit. Promoters if you're listening: it's time to
start taking some chances again. I for one will *never* return to this
space and, given recent experiences, am abandoning massives in general.

I know I've been bitching a lot lately and I'm sure many of you are sick of
it. Sorry. I'll try and shut up, put my energy where my heart is, and let
evolution take care of the dinosaurs. ;-)

take it easy
ethan

	id AA05100; Mon, 13 Jun 94 10:11:04 PDT
Date: Mon, 13 Jun 94 10:11:04 PDT
From: lxfogel@srv.PacBell.COM (Lee Fogel)
Message-Id: <9406131711.AA05100@pbssi.srv.PacBell.COM>
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: weekend report
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Friday - Ananda: We were pretty psyched for this; great DJ lineup,
outdoors, free.  We napped till 1:30, showered, and watched Beavis &
Butthead while waiting for the map point location to be given out.  
Finally, at around 3:00 or so, the location was revealed to be Ocean 
Beach, in the vicinity GG Park.  We scratched our heads in bewilderment
since this site seemed like a sure bust.  In warm weather, there are 
always people hanging out at that beach and it is always patrolled.  
Back to sleep.

Saturday - The ambient party at 174 King St. was quite enjoyable.
Consistantly excellent music, good sound, decent visuals.  YAP did
a rousing semi-live set that I just *had* to dance to, but for the
most part we just spaced out.  Hearing some of FSOL's Lifeforms played 
loud on a big system was particulary intense.  Over the entire evening 
the music seemed to leaned toward tribal/trance with slow but often 
heavy beats - great stuff.

Security was strict, but not horrible - a friend did have her pipe 
conviscated, but considering the recent SFPD activities, I can kinda 
understand this.  In fact, the SFPD did come later and swept the place 
with flashlights, eventually leaving without incident.  It was pretty 
ironic that shortly after the pipe incident, we were compelled to change
our location to escape the very heavy tabacco smokers who were 
engulfing us with a nonstop cloud of poison.  Eventually, the lack of
fresh air in that space got to us anyway, and we left around 4:30.

The thing about chillout parties is that there is a greater amount of
intimacy involved, unlike at raves were constant motion makes one
less likely to feel trapped by a localized annoyance.  There was a small
amount of sexual slithering and a couple of mouth flappers who didn't
seem to understand the meaning of the word "chill", but overall, the vibe 
was respectful and serene and quite appreciative of what was being
performed.  I would have like some more lighting effects to add to the
video/slide projector screens, but other than that, it was a very
well-produced event.  Looking forward to the next one. 

- leg of eel

1 - a note from the editor

Dear fellow pronoids--

It's been a week since the first beach head was established
here on the East Coast.  NYC is this cold, hard city, right?

Not if you're pronoid.

We've been jacked into the core of the cultural matrix in
such cauldrons as Liquid Sky, Greenwich Village, Soho and
more...  The NYC natives sense Zippies are filled with the
light side of the force.  The Death Star is doomed.

New gigs in the NYC underground scene will send us off
towards the Rocky Mountains at the end of June, and points
west.
___________________________________________________________

2 - NYC gigs

    1 - 8 p.m.  GROUNATION concert  ***FREE***

A gathering of Roots percussions and DJs united to deliver
the One Love message and vibration: all communities
represented in NYC will join in.  Drums from the Carribeans,
South America, Africa, UnitedStates, Haiti, Brazil, the
American Rainbow Family, Jamaican Nyabinghis-- and many more.
Every conscious individual is invited to bring their drum and
share in the unity for justice and peace.  An international
gathering of poets will participate.

  For info CALL/FAX Ms. Janet Rienstra: (212) 219 2060

My party impressions of the weekend.

Thursday I met some friends at Flour.
A skinny bar with a skinny dance room and a pool room in the back.
30 - 40 people dropped by while I was there.
Some were dolled up (I am a sucker for any effort).
House that wasn't perfect for the loungy crowd but improved later.
I wanted to go to the $5 bday party but we called it an early night.

Saturday we tried the chill party but wanted to dance so we didn't go in.
Then we tried the IBeam - it was $7 for hiphop but only until 2:00.
Next we went to Fundamental.  We waited in line for 15 minutes with
500 high school kids talking about grad night and yearbooks.  We left.

We drove down Howard Street and saw at least 10 cop cars and a paddy wagon
just fucking storm some club (6??).  It was like a swat team invasion as they
charged the door - we got out of the area quickly.

Dave

Weekend Rave report
===================

   This Saturday evening,   after checking out the info numbers to 
determine the locations to our big Saturday evening events,   I find
that....

  The Chill Shall Inherit the Earth was at 174 King St (one of my
      blacklisted venues - so THIS one was not a go...)
      
  Indonesia was at 16th and Harrison (Yet another blacklisted venue by
      any self respecting "Old schooler")
  
  Zig Zag/Trix was at the DV8 - Now THIS was promising,  but the DJ list
      didn't have anyone I thought I would enjoy.
      
  Fundamental - WOW!  Great DJ lineup....  But as of about 7 pm,  the
      venue wasn't put up on info line yet.
      
      
   Eventually I learn that it was at the new 19th and Alabama venue,  some
Latino Cultural center.    Hmmm!  After attending Wicked there last weekend,
I had some reservations about the very high "Faschist goon factor" or in
other words,  the security bozos were WORST than NAZI's.   Last weekend,
I was able to find a reasonable "Chill" space to cool down,  dispite the
fact that the goons had it shut tighter than a dungion,  with little
or NO ventilation and exceptionally high humidity (A Tradition with
WICKED parties -  I have NO complaints about that as long as I'm dressed
cool,  and can get some outside air during chill times).

  As I arrived (About 1:30 am),  I found the line very long and slow,   but
as I went up to the front of the line to check on the price,   I was immediately
grabbed by a group of young ravers who offerred me a place in line.   This was
promising.    All wanting to know and talk to me.    All were eager to find
out about why I'm called Cap'n Crunch.   One dude handed me inscence and
as I got to the front of the line to get searched,  the goon said I couldn't
bring the inscence inside.   Sheesh!!  What the fuck...  do they really think
I was going to burn the place down?  ...with all the tobacco smoking going on.

  Inside... It was PIG CITY,  as Mayor Frank Jordan was keeping to his obsession
to "Clean up SOMA (South of Market Area)".   As usual,  it was crowded,  and
a little hard to move around in the narrow hallways to go between rooms.   The
only water source was the wash basin in the over-crowded mens room.

  This week,  they had stationed a goon near the door,  so ALL doorways were
"Gooned" I would say.    Ocasionally,  I would lean on the door,  and 
"Accidentely" lean on it too hard to get even just ONE gasp of fresh air,
but was warned that I would get kicked out the next time I committed the
evil and hidious crime of breathing fresh air.

   Later on,  I discovered an open door behind the projection equipment,
situated on a stage like area.   In this little room,  the had some chairs
and a big wide open window,  letting in some nice and welcome fresh air.
I noticed this after I hopped onto the stage and discovered a nice cool
breeze and traced it to its origin.

  The sound SUX big time....  Horribly distorted,  almost an embarrassment
to the great efforts of the DJ's which tried to deal with it.   There were
two rooms.   One small (Which Buck was spinning) and had tinney, and crappy
sound with NO bass.   In the larger room,  I found Garth cooking up a
wonderful trancey brew (As he always does).   My energy level,  turned up to
the MAX (As Usual) was highly instrumental in generating a great number
of smiles and good vibes in a venue that is somewhat lacking in same.

  I eventually leave around 6 am,  where I was to get picked up to help
my partner Aaron get ready to run the Dipsey Trail,  a 7 mile run from
Mill Valley to Stinson Beach over a part of Mt Tamalpias.    It's an
85 year tradition,  but this time,  I passed on the opportunity.
Aaron did it in 1 hr 10 mins (record was 45 minutes).   Exceptionally
good.    Some 68 yr old dude named "Sal" won it (3 times so far,  as I
was told.

  Eventually,  we head back into SF to hang out at the End up for a few
hours so Aaron could use the car to visit with his friends from out of town.

  Later that afternoon we head out to the Haight St fair and had a killer time
hanging out and was also invited to Ameba's (A rave related clothing store on
the Haight) backyard party.    It was KILLER!!   About 300 people were there
when I arrived,   and Garth was dishing out some insane funk,  mixed with
some killer trance that blew my mind.   The dance area Sucked,  was very 
uneven ground,   but the luv factor was turned on to the Max,  and it
was a very happy scene.   Exceptional sound,  and had a great time dancing
my ass off (OR TRYING TO).

   Later on,  it was moved up the I-Beam,   a very large night club,  good
ventilation,  and reasonable sound.    We eventually left around 9:30 pm,
and head back North over the Golden Gate,  back into Marin Co.

   All in All,  it was a wonderful weekend,  although my knees were complaining
today from dancing on the uneven ground.

Till next time...  Keep the scene alive...

CC

I was SO RELIEVED to read the negative reviews of Fundamental.
Until I read those reviews, I thought that this event might be
representative of the entire san francisco scene.  A few additional 
comments:  At 1:30 the line was the longest line I have ever
seen for a house club, so I went down the street to Indonesia.
Indonesia had good production (sound system and projections
were top-notch), but it lacked any real vibe.  The crowd
seemed more high-school aged... which by itself is not bad at all,
but I think they were the high school kids who don't have a clue.  
At 4:30 I went
back to Fundamental, only to find nasty argument between
the promoter, the venue manager, and a few DJ's (including
Ernie Munson).  Apparently it was an "I gave you the money/no you
did not" thing.  No one wanted to take my 10 bucks, so I just walked
in.  A few people up in the house room were pretty cool, and we kind
of produced our own little vibe, but then (excuse my language)
the most FUCKED UP thing I have ever seen at a club happened.
This guy kept dancing around the floor, being real annoying and 
bothersome.  A girl stopped him and (I assume) asked him to 
to dance in a way that didn't disturb others.  A small shouting
match ensued, and he shoved her clear across the floor.  She barely
kept her balance, only for him to come up to her, and start yelling
and threatening her.  A friend of his quickly stopped him.  What an
awful thing to witness on my first weekend in SF.
	The weekend wasn't all bad though.  I thought Anada was very
cool.  Renegade parties on the beach is something you don't see
in southern cal.
The music was hard-trancish, and the climate was relatively warm,
thanks to record-heat on friday (56' at 3:30am.)  Certainly the
most fun I have had on the beach for a while.  I'm still 
pulling sand out of my Vans, though. :)
	Also, on Thursday I found Lift to be fun.  Good house music, 
about 30-50 people dancing, and generally happy attitudes.  This is a 
good club for a Thursday night (the vibe was certainly higher than
anything I went to on Saterday night)

-troy

Subject:  Who's breakbeat? -Reply

	One thing that will help you tell breakbeat is that it's generally
really fast... about 150 + beats per minute.  You probably don't hear
very much of it on the west coast, it isn't very popular there. 
Typically the way people make breakbeat is they take a house beat,
and speed it up to double speed, then they take this double-speed
beat, and play it at 150 bpm or so, so that's where all the
syncopation comes from.  You might notice chipmunk-like voices in
some breakbeat, because some breakbeat djs like to play their 33 rpm
records at 45, giving it that "double-speed chipmunks on acid" type
sound...  One type of breakbeat that's very popular in England right
now is called Jungle.  It's based on reggae music that's been sped up
quite a bit...  I'm not very into breakbeat, but Jungle is pretty
cool.  By no means am I an expert on the subject, so if anyone cares
to correct me, feel free.

>>> Larry Ching <larryc@netcom.com>  6/11/94, 12:01pm >>>

Lady Trash asks:

>I am still confused by one of Laura's statements that UK "hardcore" is 
>like US "breakbeat". I really thought they  were totally different

It is a bit confusing.  Breakbeat and hardcore (US definition) are quite
different.  What the English call "hardcore" is what people in the US 
call "breakbeat." What people in the US call "hardcore" is what the English 
call "Rotterdam" or sometimes "Gabber."  

In the UK:  hardcore is different from Rotterdam
in the US:  breakbeat is different from hardcore

'I say elevator, you say lift
I say trunk, you say boot
let's call the whole thing off' :-) :-)

Laura

I wonder how much most breaks are directly related to house beats, which
typically are in the 115-130 bpm range.  Ragga and jungle both depend
on reggae riddims which are often in the 70-85 bpm range which conveniently
doubles to the 140-170 range favored for breaks and jungle.

As for faster beats, I'm a contrarian, I've been known to play faster
45s at 33 and 'Autobahn' at 45 :-)

Rather than batting around verbal descriptions of musical genres, I find
that actual examples usually work a lot better.  Here's what I would consider
to be good examples of some of the genres that have been asked about lately...

progressive house: Get any of the "Cream of Undergound House" compilations.
	There are three volumes so far.  All of them are good examples of
	what I would consider to be progressive house.  Unfortunately they
	are imports from the UK, which means they're a bit expensive.  For
	cheaper (domestic) progressive house compilations, I would recommend
	Epic Records' "Futurhythm" compilation or Profile Records' "Future
	House" compilation.

breakbeat: I'm not an expert on this one, but I've seen lots of recommendations
	for Moonshine Music's "Speed Limit 140 bpm+" series of compilations.
	(These are all domestic and pretty easy to find.)

house: The best house CD I have ever heard is a DJ-mixed CD called "Spiritual
	Tracks Volume 1."  It's an import and may be hard to find.  (There's
	also a "Spiritual Tracks Volume 2", which isn't quite as good as #1.)

trance: Get "Trance Europe Express."  This is an import, but it's not over-
	priced at all.  You get 2 full-length CDs and a 200-page booklet that
	has interviews with the featured artists, all for only $22 or so.

tribal: Get Twitch CD #6.

If you're searching for any of the above CDs, I'd suggest starting out by
calling BPM (415-567-0BPM) or Tweekin' (415-626-6995).

Subject: Re: Who's breakbeat? -Reply
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

For a good breakbeat sample that many people on this list probably all now,
get your Exist Dance compilations out and listen to the beats in High
Lonesome Sound System's "Psychic Dreaming".  This is much slower than you
normally hear for breakbeat.

>Typically the way people make breakbeat is they take a house beat,
>and speed it up to double speed, then they take this double-speed
>beat, and play it at 150 bpm or so, so that's where all the
>syncopation comes from.

Actually, I'm pretty sure the beats in breakbeat are sped up hip-hop beats.

I was in England when breakbeat (which they called hardcore at the time
because it was so fast) was taking off and many DJs were just taking
hip-hop records that played at 33rpm but they played them at 45rpm.  That's
why the vocal samples sound like "the chipmunks".  I don't think breakbeat
has changed much since '91.  It's only gotten faster.

Hi -

re:
>Does anyone know anything about the Oregon Country Fair. I've picked up a few
>interesting comments about it from here and there and it's got me interested.

The 25th annual OCF is Fri, Sat, Sun July 8,9,10 (always 2nd weekend in
July) on a site owned by OCF approx 15 miles west of Eugene.  I think the
hours are 11am to 7 or 8 pm.

Friday is usually fresher and less crowded, but starting last year they
have limited the number of tickets sold for each day (several thousand) and
tightened up on the IDs for staff/vendors/etc who have overnight access. 
Tickets ( $7 Friday, $10 Sat & Sun?) can be purchased in advance (if
interested, I'll try to find more info).  There is no camping or overnight
parking on the grounds.  Free busses run regularly from/to Eugene.

Much fun! (from my biased perspective as a 50 year old who has attended
approx every other year since 1975 or so).  Colorful! When we lived in
rural Oregon the fair was THE event of the year.  A large main stage/dance
area and several small stages with variety of music all day.  A drum area
with constant drumming and dancing.  Food (try Tofu Tia special). Crafts.
Massage. Community village.  Alternative energy.  Layout is a large figure
8 trail with side loops.  One of my favorite off-the-main path (often
missed) attraction for relaxation is the Ritz sauna with large group
outdoor showers and firepit gathering area (often live music); usually only
available ($3) until 3pm? for fair attendees.

Usually good music (Radiators and rave this year?) in Eugene area that weekend.

Enjoy.

- Ed

I went to my first Country Fair last year and had a b-l-a-s-t!  I'm going 
up again this year. Don't get your hopes up for a rave on the grounds, 
though.  Preston talked to them about it last year, and despite the 
appeal of another alternative culture, the technology/electronic nature 
of the thing seemed to scare them.  I was walking around with Mark Farina 
who was playing beats on a boom box, and despite the fact that he 
recevied a lot of smiles and knowing winks, some people working for the 
fair asked him to turn it off.  :(

If you can go, go.  If you can't, don't.


Tony

Dear Sindar,

    I'm sorry it's taken so long to reply to this, but I'm *way* behind 
on reading my email.  I just came across your post (above) responding to 
my review of Spundae's last month, and I think you deserve an explanation 
of my feelings on this.  Talking about illegal actions being committed 
was not an unintentional "mistake" on my part; I have thought about this 
issue before, and I am comfortable with my approach.  Before I go on to 
explain why, I want to thank you for the positive and non-judgemental 
tone of your message, which I will strive to maintain.
    I too, by the way, am over 21 -- I just happen not to have any 
picture ID as a result of having my wallet and my passport stolen on two 
separate occasions, one of which I regret to say was at a small, intimate 
rave.
    But anyway, to the point.  I am aware of the fact that theoretically 
anyone, including law enforcement personnel, could be reading the sfraves 
mail.  I don't think this is particularly likely, considering the size of 
the list, its lack of visibility, and the fact that the SFPD has many 
other things to worry about, but even if I knew for a fact that some 
government official was poring over my posts, I don't think I would 
delete any references to illegal activities.
    This month marks the 25th anniversary of the Stonewall riots in New 
York, a historical event whose significance is perhaps just beginning to 
be recognized on a broad scale.  This was, in effect, when gays started 
to come out of the closet in modern times.  I can easily imagine in 
pre-Stonewall times a lot of conversations taking place along the lines 
of:  "You better watch your mouth!  I overheard you telling those guys 
about the gay scene at our bar, and you never know who could be 
listening.  The cops have had their eye on this place, you know, and if 
word starts getting around that it's a homosexual pickup joint, we'll get 
busted!"
    Do you see my point?  Laws against drug use by adults and laws 
forbidding people under a certain age to enter certain establishments are 
as wrong as laws against certain types of sexual activity.  Bad laws 
deserve to be broken, and in fact these laws are broken regularly.  But 
the #1 weapon in the arsenal of the authorities who want to tell us how 
to live our lives is our own silence about our behavior.
    To return to the example of gay rights, as long as gays remained "in 
the closet," and broke the unjust laws against same-sex relations only 
covertly, it was relatively easy for the bigots to keep them in their 
status as second-class citizens.  Only when gays stood up for their 
rights openly, and confronted the law head-on did they achieve real 
change.  
    The same unwritten code of silence exists today in regard to drug use 
and many other "victimless crimes."  Now maybe I am not brave enough (or 
martyr enough) to get up and say, "Hey, I'm in this club, and I'm using 
Exstasy.  What are you going to do about it?" to a cop, and when I was 
under 21 I didn't advertise that fact when I got into a bar, but I am 
brave enough to speak out publicly on the fact that these things go on, 
and I am a willing participant.  What this does is build momentum, and 
create a stronger consensus in the community of what 99% of us already 
know is true:  that these laws are unjust, and deserve to be broken.  
When enough of us get up and say that, and refuse to be denied our human 
rights any longer, then things will change.  I look forward to that day.

"You can stop the party, but you can't stop the future."

"You can pledge allegiance to the flag -- I pledge allegiance to freedom."

                          *** Starchild ***

Thank you, Starchild, for so eloquently raising the issue
of the immorality of bad laws and the imperative for each           
one of us to break them to the extent that we can!

Thank you, too, Sindar, for giving Starchild the opportunity
to address the issue! Each of us must go as far as we are
comfortable in confronting immorality. At a recent party I
attended last week in the City, whilst enjoying one of the
most spiritually evolved djs I've had the pleasure to dance
to, it became obvious to me and others that at least two
narcs were present, one who was chain-drinking bar drinks,
blowing continual blasts of smoke in dancers' faces and
lurking continuously in front of a speaker stack.  In my
heightened state of awareness it gave me a surge of hyperkarma
to stand next to this moral neanderthal and stare at him
until he became aware of me (about one and a half minutes)
and then calmly tell him that it takes much less effort to
respect others' rights to enjoy the music, breathe the air,
and dance without being stared at, and that one really has
to work at being an asshole. He left his unfinished drink on    
the speaker, smashed his cigarette under his heel, nattered
something about this being his kind of music, too, and stormed
off the dance floor--for awhile.  Mine was just a minor and
random act of poetic terrorism, but as a person who has come
to see that the closets I have been walking out of are largely
self-created (even though they are constructed by our immoral
culture) I believe my "coming out" to him was a positive and
entheogenic epiphany for both of us.

I hope Starchild and Sindar have touched a topic that will
kindle at least a minor thread here, because even if this
subject has been visited before, and especially because it
makes some sfr people uneasy, it remains pivotal to our
very being in the "rave community."  The comparison to
Stonewall and gays is apt; as a gay man whose own self-
oppression has been the most crucial immoral judgment laid
down by an unjust society I know that--as is etched in my
high school's marble entry walls where some of the names of    
the dead are former students of mine--"Freedom Cometh Not Free!"

World's second oldest raver,
Will

Will Penna               408.423 8907

is the dance of creation.

Oh yeah, and for everyone who posted and said "I'm so sorry I missed 
Laura at 'In the Light'" -- I'm fairly sure I'm spinning first so
get there at the beginning!  None of this "fashionably late" stuff:
you KNOW that Ethan, Bryce, and crew have their act together and
that the set-up will ocurr on time, but the party REALLY doesn't get 
going until people start showing up, so don't hesitate, come on
down at 10:00 pm!  If you get there at the beginning, you can also
catch a live performance by Weird Blinking Lights who are opening up
in the Chill Room. 

See you there!

Laura

From sfraves-owner  Thu Jun 16 12:02:30 1994

To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU

Subject: Re: breakbeat
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Breakbeat is most likely called breakbeat because it uses breaksbeats.  I
suspect that the Brits call it hardcore because breaks are nothing new, its
just a very hard fast form of breakbeat driven music.  I suspect many
Americans went straight from synth/drum machine house to hearing the British
hardcore sound and the most indentifiable element was the double-speed
breakbeats.  What's a break beat anyway?  It's the part of a song where
everone takes a break except the drummer(who didn't need to light up a cig
anyway.)  You know, James Brown says" Break it down" and the players slowly
drop out till you get that killer 2-bar break with just the drummer which is
perfect for sampling. The earliest disco DJs first started extending songs by
buying two copies of the record and alternating between the two to make the
break section go on and on and on - yeah.  Its the life blood of hip-hop and
most house, while often not using breaks,  was influeneced by the sound these
early DJs created.   Lots of the big anthemic, over-the-top tracks of the
late 80s/early 90s used breaks too.  The 33/45 thing has been going on for a
long time, but jungle/hardcore breakbeat went double-speed on the break often
accompanied by a dive-bomb near-subsonic sine tone bass and chipmunk vocals.
 The later stuff used insanely sliced up snippets of breaks (half a bar or
less at double, regular or other speeds) that usually don't start on the beat
the orginal break started on.  In a very long tradition of copying our
American talent, many of the British tracks get their breaks and sometimes
vocals off the latest hip-hop tracks.  Hope that helps.

Greetings Friends!

Aside from an obsessive compulsion to absolutely bury you in hype ;-) two
things have prompted me to issue this final invitation to Friends & Family.

The first is that numerous people have been sending me email asking for
details on a variety of topics; so I hope I can now answer all your
questions.

The second is that, last week, I noticed in the introduction to the
calendar that, counting both the calendar and the main list, there are now
more than 900 of us here! I personally know maybe 100 of you. So I thought
it might be nice tp provide, for the other 800 of you, some history -- the
context in which this party occurs and also introduce those of you who
don't already know us to the people involved in this party. 

Back in December on a lovely Sunday afternoon Bryce and I (and some of you)
threw the second of two indoor Liquid Airs at he 3rd Wave Dance House in
the mission. The first one had been very well attended and we had high
hopes for the second; it featured a great line-up, was in a wonderful
space, and had been (we thought) well promoted. 

Well, nobody came. We were very disappointed. So much so that we took our
dissapointment to the list expressing our belief that this "community" had
let us down by not supporting what we had intended to be a community and
specifically an *sfr* party. Needless to say this sparked an impassioned
debate on the list as to whether we (on this list) are in fact a community
or merely a group of people that use email like we use telephones, like we
use cars etc. 

Out of the untold *skads* of feedback we received, one thing became clear:
if you want to do a "community" party, you've got to actively *involve* the
community and in turn the community has to actively involve itself. I think
I can safely say that since then, Bryce and I have tried to let this idea
be the guiding light in our party coordinating efforts.

The next party that (the now greatly expanded) 'we' threw was the first
Friends & Family. As the name suggests it was intended to be, and was, a
massive celebration of this most intimate relation we share: friends,
family, community.

And what a night it was! For 12 solid hours the Blue Cube, nestled in the
heart of residential Noe Valley, *rocked hard* without *one* complaint.
Truly, that night we opened up and disappeared into a deep and acidic
ripple in spacetime...Down in the bassment laura's laser sparkled on the
sfr banner while upstairs in the kitchen live ambient trance, deep dub and
house bubbled among the salsa and the pretzels !-) Out on the porch,
shrouded in the densest fog I've ever seen, two didjeridoos added their
voices to the evening...all in all, well over 14 musicians/djs -- many from
sfr -- but others as well, played that night. So many people helped flier,
helped set up, brought lights, brought friends, brought their postitve
energy. Yeewoooow. What a party.

Lets do it again.

You,Me:Us:We: Friends & Family

When: Saturday, June 18th, 10pm til at least 7am
Where: Komotion: 16th at Folsom in SF -- *not* the Haze Theatre
Why: Because we love you :)
More info: 415.985.5244
Who's welcome: *Everyone*
What can you bring inside: *anything*
Cost: $3 benefits the space (Komotion) *entirely*
Dance Music: Laura, Alex, Lee, Ethan, Tamotsu, spun
Ambience: Weird Blinking Lights, Joe Rice, HDW, M, Ronan
Ambient Guided Visualisation: M & Ovid
Visuals & Lighting: Donovan, John Martinko, Sean Casey

Lots of you have been asking if you can bring fruit, toys, candy etc. The
answer is YES! YES! YES! *Please* bring lots of fruit, toys, candy,
positive energy, beanbags, pillows, cushions and other chill gear plus
anything else you think might be fun. Also, please dress in cool clothes
(No. temperature you geek ;-) boxers & brassiers recommended) and COME
EARLY!

And, one final note: WE NEED PEOPLE TO HELP SET UP! There're speakers that
need carrying, floors that need sweeping, couches that need moving, banners
that need hanging...we're going to get there around 6:00 to get started; if
you can come then or thereafter please let me know as soon as possible. 

On that subject: I need at least one person to volunteer to help me get the
sound system from bryce's (in SF) around 5:00pm; he's in SoCal til Saturday
and should his plane get delayed we'd be *screwed* as there's no way I can
lift those suckers myself...


We've done our absolute best to get as many people involved in this party
as possible, and I think the results are going to be spectacular! So
please, join us: bring your magic, your energy, your love and lets take
this party right off the deep end. I truly look forward to meeting all of
you there!

lots of love
ethan

You know, I really like discussing music, even if it is the questionable
pursuit of trying to define  genres.  I have yet to find a good list for
this(talking about the music we love, not defing genres.)  This list has so
much traffic that a continuous discussion of the music is probably too much,
the analogue synthesizer list is overly concerned with the equipment, the bpm
dj list strangely has very little on the actual content/intent of songs.  Is
there a list I'm missing?  I was looking for something more than, "I got the
new xxxxxx. It's really good, you should get it."  It really is possible to
discuss music with intelligence and depth, though sample snippets would be
cool.   This list does an amazing job of capturing the feel of the scene, a
seriously nebulous, hard-to-express entity if there ever was one, in text
format .

I want to start this post by saying how much respect I have for anyone who 
legitimizes gay rights by "coming out of the closet" and putting themselves 
in a position of rejection and even possible violence for personal freedom.  
I would, however, have much less respect for someone who forces others 
"out" when they may not be ready.  This brings me to the point of naming a 
particular club as one where drugs are bought openly.  Now, the club owner,
the promoter as well as other club goers are thrown into a position that
they may not want to deal with especially with today's South of Market   
climate.  There are so many ways to show support for the legalization or 
decriminalization of drugs, i.e., starting or signing petitions, marching 
on City Hall/Washington, D.C. or writing letters to people who are in a
position to help.  Openly talking about paying $20 for a hit of MDMA after
getting in without valid ID as being a courageous way to make change, in my
opinion, is NOT. 

janie

Thanks, Janie, for focusing us on another--and 
immediately important--aspects of SOMA, clubs, cops
and closets! We hould clarify our intentions in communicating,
whether to ourselves or with others! While I know what I
am doing is not immoral, it is still illegal!  What a
paradox--just like it used to be what I was was a mortal
sin and a "crime against nature" in California courtts!  
I took the esoteric road, the inward path out, and it took
almost 50 years and I still see the cave opening only as an
occasional magic moment when ego becomes eco and harm
becomes herm. Perhaps the openly committed have to rant as
well as rave, eh?  Both "voices" are hard to hear, and I
admit I incline toward the path your message suggests, the
path of the heart, not just of the spirit *or* the soul,
a path that includes all, inclusiveness being the way of
karma.
Part I'm responding to most, from Janie:

There are so many ways to show support for the legalization or
decriminalization of drugs, i.e., starting or signing petitions, marching
on City Hall/Washington, D.C. or writing letters to people who are in a
position to help.  Openly talking about paying $20 for a hit of MDMA after
getting in without valid ID as being a courageous way to make change, in my
opinion, is NOT.

>responding to 
>my review of Spundae's last month, and I think you deserve an >explanation 
>of my feelings on this.  Talking about illegal actions being >committed 
>was not an unintentional "mistake" on my part; I have thought >about this 
>issue before, and I am comfortable with my approach.  Before >I go on to 
>explain why, I want to thank you for the positive and >non-judgemental 
>tone of your message, which I will strive to maintain.

>picture ID as a result of having my wallet and my passport >stolen on two 
>separate occasions, one of which I regret to say was at a >small, intimate

>    But anyway, to the point.  I am aware of the fact that >theoretically

Well I think that the SFPD has demonstrated to some degree that they do not
have anything better to do...  Look at what is going on with the SOMA thing.
 If I were an investigative reporter for ABC or a cop whose job was to do
nothing but infiltrate the "evil" club/rave scene (which I am NOT) I might
catch on to a conection between the computer and the scene in SF.  The Net
will with out a doubt tell you at least what is going on and a little bit
about who's who.  It would certianly be easier than actually doing it the old
way...  Well in truth I do not really think that SF Raves is a big thing to
these people but it would seem that if they were smart and wanted to know
what was going on this would not be a bad place to start.  I mean these
people (reporters and cops) have been known to go thru peoples trash and love
it... I do agree with you that openess could help bring down these really
lame laws.  I have thought long and hard about ways to dissmantle the current
system that puts out these neggative commandments.  Taking out these laws
would in my view be a very good thing...  personally I believe that it is
drug laws and not drugs that cause most of the "scurge of drugs".  I will
stand by my origional point which was that I think that even though it is
good to be public, sometimes it is just as good to not show all of your cards
just yet.  More than my thinking about the police I worried that you were
spreading the word that Spundae was a club who let in minors.  Of course if
they did then that is there own fault, but because I would rather the place
remain open I would not try to swamp the place with minors who heard they
could get in thus putting Spundae at risk even if it was by there own
stupidity.  On a different slant of Spundae...  I was thinking about how
Spundae has lost a lot of it's origional more friendly crowd...  I mean the
crowd is still great as far as most club clubs go but it might make things a
little bit fresher if more SF Ravers started showing up.  No I don't work at
Spundae although I may be performing at Spundae latter this summer I'll let
you know.  8 )

 RE: Outer Rhythm Records , a techno vinyl store in West San Jose 

 Scott Nozawa recommended this store in a recent posting - I was just 
there today , and I'll have to eagerly second his recommendation! They 
seem to have a lot of the latest vinyl , including GAK , Future
Sound Of London's Lifeform , The Dust Brother's "My Mercury Mouth" ,
Courtney Nielsen & DJ Spun's "Central Fire" on Twitch Records , and
other stuff. Finally , a good techno vinyl source in San Jose! 

 Three previewing turntables for the customers, and a friendly staff
( at least the guy I talked to was OK ).

 The store itself is very unobtrusive , and mislabelled to boot! It used
to be a car stereo installation and sales store , and the old sign
is still on the roof ( "Mobile Audio" or some such ). It's at 
368 South Bascom Avenue , a few doors south of the notorious Pink
Poodle strip club , near the intersection of Bascom Avenue and San 
Carlos . They're open until 9PM Mon - Fri , until 8PM on the weekends
( call ahead to confirm these hours ).
 

 The ironic thing is - I used to live in the house behind the store -
but I've just moved out! I live in Sunnyvale now - but San Jose is still
closer than San Francisco or Berkeley. I'll be doing most of my shopping
for vinyl at Outer Rhythm before I try up north.

	Larry Ching/larryc@netcom.com

i am proud to announce the song line-up for the upcoming NETherworld tape-
there was so much high quality stuff sent to me that i am still in awe!so,
without further ado, the NETherworld lineup (in no particular order):

1. axon "pygme up"
2. symbion project "the infinite number of truths that remain to be discovered"
2. method one "new day"
4. john sweeney "phylum"
5. logarithmic sound source "biogene" (genesplice mix)
6. glowball "tripping backwards"
7. induction "106"
8. audio tribe "vision quest"
9. offworld "etheria"
10.kingsize "cocopuff"
11.tintinnabulation "mantis"
12.1.8.7. "jungleman" (wicked jungle mix)
13.sean simmen "blue skies"
14.francois dion "geoide"

i think there might also be a song from one of taylor's projects, but like an id
   iot i forgot to mail him.....so im not sure aboout it

due to space limitations, iwasn't able to use all the songs sent to me-to
all who didn't get in, dont worry....there will be a netherworld 2 at some
point :)

to all those who DID get in-there are a few things i need from you:
1. i need a good copy of the song that was accepted.-completly produced, on
no less than a type II (high bias) cassette. unfortunatly, i wont have
access to a DAT machine like i first planned...but i can make high quality
tape copies, so if you send a good-sounding cassette to me, the song will
still sound good in the comp. now, if you think that the version you sent
me already is produced well enough, let me know and you wont have to send
me a new tape. remember, you are basically responsibe for how your tracks sound,
so make sure it is good :)

2. for the tape insert, i need a mini bio from all of you: name, song title,
e-mail and snail mail addresses, people involved, and all that. feel free
to add any other info, like shout outs, equipment list, sayings, proverbs,
whatever you want to say...just dont make it too long (about a good paragraph)

3. please get me the master copies AS SOON AS POSSIBLE!!!i wanna actually
stArt producing these things in say, mid july

On Wed, 15 Jun 1994, Starchild wrote:
> busted!"
>     Do you see my point?  Laws against drug use by adults and laws 
> forbidding people under a certain age to enter certain establishments are 
> as wrong as laws against certain types of sexual activity.  Bad laws 
> deserve to be broken, and in fact these laws are broken regularly.  But 
> the #1 weapon in the arsenal of the authorities who want to tell us how 
> to live our lives is our own silence about our behavior.
>     To return to the example of gay rights, as long as gays remained "in 
> the closet," and broke the unjust laws against same-sex relations only 
> covertly, it was relatively easy for the bigots to keep them in their 
> status as second-class citizens.  Only when gays stood up for their 
> rights openly, and confronted the law head-on did they achieve real 
> change.  
>     The same unwritten code of silence exists today in regard to drug use 
> and many other "victimless crimes."  Now maybe I am not brave enough (or 
> martyr enough) to get up and say, "Hey, I'm in this club, and I'm using 
> Exstasy.  What are you going to do about it?" to a cop, and when I was 
> under 21 I didn't advertise that fact when I got into a bar, but I am 
> brave enough to speak out publicly on the fact that these things go on, 
> and I am a willing participant.  What this does is build momentum, and 
> create a stronger consensus in the community of what 99% of us already 
> know is true:  that these laws are unjust, and deserve to be broken.  
> When enough of us get up and say that, and refuse to be denied our human 
> rights any longer, then things will change.  I look forward to that day.
> 
> "You can stop the party, but you can't stop the future."
> 
> "You can pledge allegiance to the flag -- I pledge allegiance to freedom."
> 
>                           *** Starchild ***
> 
	I am really glad to see someone else tackle the drug issue 
headon.  The comparison Starchild has made of talking about drugs and 
talking about homosexuality in an open forum backs up my firm standing on 
the issue:  just because drugs are "illegal" does not mean they are 
"wrong".  I believe the fundamental problem with the drug issue is that 
too many people have been fooled into believing that drugs=wrong=lack of 
family values=have to get rid of drugs because they are what is wrong 
with our society today.  

	If you check your history books, people throughout time have 
"broken the law" because what they believed in was more important.  In 
the pre-Civil war years, the underground railroad "illegally" freed 
thousands of slaves and brought them to the North.  The masters had full 
legal rights to go reclaim their property.  Was this freeing of people 
from oppression "right" or "wrong"?  That question is up to each 
individual to answer for themselves.  However you choose to answer that 
question, though, you still cannot escape from one fact.  People who 
cared enough about the well-being of others broke the law to protect 
them; more importantly, enough people (or at least the right ones) said 
this law was wrong and abolished slavery.  

	There are many other examples in history where people 
broke the law to stand up for what they believe in.  The women's 
movement, the Civil Rights Movement, Ghandi and his followers are some 
examples.  What about the complete disregard in this country of 
Prohibition?  Do you really think anyone who liked drinking alcohol in 
those times were going to stop drinking just because the government 
suddenly said it was wrong?  

	Anyway, I seem to have much more to say about this subject, but 
rather than make this a 10-page email that you probably won't read, I 
will make this message as short as a "sound bite".  I hope I've made my 
point about this.  We cannot go around fearing what the government will 
do to us, although we don't want to go right up to the law and spit in 
its face.  Times are changing.  I can see it around me.  People are 
realizing that drugs are no big deal for the most part, and the more you 
restrict people from doing them, the more they will want to do them.  

Look for future articles from me, deepfog.

DJ FOG

--end transmission--

Subject: Friends, Family & The Universe
Cc: sfraves-planners@techno.Stanford.EDU
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

Since the dawn of human knowledge, we homosapiens have been trancing out
to music, feeling our conenctiveness to the forces and cycles of nature, 
becoming conscious of how these forces also exist within ourselves;
forces that have meaning beyond the limits of our lives, like spirituality.
Ultimately, there is no difference between science and spirituality, no
difference between raving and being connected to the essence of existence.
It all comes down to how aware we want to be about it.  

SFRavers come from all walks of life, and this is one of the things that 
makes this information crossroad a unique and enriching, as well as 
volatile, place to interact.  We are very fortunate to have Ovid Jacob
amongst us, a Theoretical Physicist from Stanford.  I'd like to encourage 
any knowledge seekers or reality surfers out there to participate in the 
visualization and discussion Ovid plans to lead at Friends & Family this 
Saturday.  In addition to getting his Phd. in Physics from  Princeton 
University, Ovid is well versed in various world religions and 
philosophies, and has given talks on some of these topics.  My 
understanding is that rather than explore the intricacies of Physics, we 
will be taken on a journey that will explore some of the modes of thinking 
and experience that surround our connections to science, philosophy and 
raving.  

Ovid will probably be a little annoyed at me for this post, for he insists
that this is not about him at all, nor does he feel that knowing about
his "credentials" are important.  But I just wanted to make sure that 
people understood that this will not just be the ramblings of a space cadet 
on a soapbox.  With M Normal providing an ambient backdrop, this will be an 
opportunity for us to combine the rave experience with an exercise in mind 
expansion; sometime between 3 and 4am in the chill room of Friends & Family.
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
Lee Fogel/\/\/\/\/\eVerything/\Is/\possiBlE/\/\/\/\/\lxfogel@srv.pacbell.com

It's been a few days but we wanted to thank all you ravers who came to 
the party here during the Haight st fair...so thank you.  Spiral jive set 
up the sound in the back yard and it was pumping--We even had some crazed 
lunatic neighbor run out onto the street in his underwear demanding all

day.  Allen & I spent most of the day at the ameba booth BUT Bahg, DRC, 
Tracy and Garth spun and the vibes are still floating around out there.

they thanked us so we're thanking you.  Later on the party moved to the 
I-Beam where David spun a mind blowingly superb set...Basically, all I

From: Tony V Garcia <deepfog@cats.ucsc.edu>
Subject: Tone's review of MESS
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Cc: deepfog@cats.ucsc.edu
Message-Id: <Pine.3.89.9406180730.A29208-0100000@si.UCSC.EDU>
Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

	Ok, listen everyone, Mother Earth on June 17th was a great party. 
It was just the kind of party that doesn't come around too often, and the
best part about it was it was GOON-FREE. 

	Of course, there were many other good things about it, too.  The
location was great.  An undisclosed location somewhere north of the now
world renowned Bonny Doon sat the sound system on a little clearing next
to the cliffs about 400 feet above the beach.  The view was spectacular
here, folks, and the nice thing about it was you could walk right from the
dance floor to the cliffs to watch the waves come in.  The waves were
really small from our bird's eye view.    

	The music was typical sfrave music at its best.  When I got there
at 5:15 (right when the sun was cracking), it was thumpin house, and then
about a half hour later when I started to get tired (no pick-me-ups for
fog today), a couple of dj's (maddie told me one of them was drew) did
some killer mixes of trippy acidhouse with lots of percussionary beats and
other stuff.  That woke me up real quick.  I thought the soundsystem was
really nice, too.  It sounded really clear for the amount and size of the
speakers.  

	I think the people was what topped it off.  When we were walking 
to the party (and believe me, we walked quite a way to get there) we 
could tell it was going to be a good party just because of the size and 
the type of people.  Jason said it reminded him of the full moons he went 
to when he first started going:  35, 40 people at the most.  Good vibes.  
Smiling people, attitude free.  Everyone may or may not have been on e.  
It didn't matter, because everyone was just happy there and COEXISTING 
with their neighbors (isn't that what we are all raving for?)  :)  It was 
really nice for me to see a fellow raver picking up trash at our party 
site.  Another guy was handing out incense to everyone.  People have 
always been the most important part of a rave, and this crowd was great.  
I don't run around meeting people as much as I used to when I first 
started partying (my first was Sharon in Sept or Oct 1991), but I mostly 
just smiled back at people here.  Reminds me of the old days.  

	So anyway, this party was just right.

Just more of these forwards... if you know your mail From: header
is going to be different, please let me know or change your
address on the list.

Before they begin, though, I thought I would let you know that 
techno.stanford.edu is going away.  Stanford is finally asking
to reclaim their Sparc 1+ and the disk space and processing power
the list and the archive takes up.  Fortunately, we don't have to
scramble for a new home, as a long-time dream of mine is about to
come true - I will be setting up a machine on the net entirely
my own in about 2 weeks called hyperreal.com, and its sole mission
will be to support hypermedia development in the online community
(ew, that reeked of cliche terms, but it's true! :)  The SFRaves
list will live there (in fact, I may be able to CNAME it to 
sfraves.org :) as will the IDM list, and the related sublists - 
the archive will also be there, and I'll be able to give out a
few accounts to people willing to maintain parts of the archives
and put up projects of their own.  It won't be a for-profit machine,
if I do any revenue-generation on it it'll go into paying for
the capital costs and upkeep.  It'll be connected to the net via
T1 from the Little Garden, sharing bandwidth with Wired Magazine.
I'm putting a down payment on the machine tomorrow - a Pentium
with 16 megs of memory and 2 gig drive running BSDI - and I should
have it fully online in two weeks.

I'll send out details and move the list over when it's up and stable.
Until then, if you have some web-related non-commercial (though if
you're a commercial artist it might be okay) projects you'd like to
put up on the web, or have ideas for new web-related software you'd
like to work on, develop them and as hyperreal comes online let me
know if you want an account.  There are some Very Interesting Guests
lined up for the system, too.  :)

Anyways, on with the forwards.

From: harden@HEDGEHOG.ICS.COM (Aub Harden)
Newsgroups: comp.windows.x.announce
Subject: Call for BoFs at Xhibition 94

 ...

For more info on the show, call '1.800.234.XHIB', send mail to 
'xhibit@ics.com', or use Mosaic to open 'URL: http//www.ics.com/'.  

Free Passes: 

Free Passes to the Tradeshow, Industry Forum, Keynote, Plenary, and BoFs 
are available via email and the Internet at the email and URL sites 
mentioned above.


Keynote: Alvin Toffler, June 22
+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

Alvin Toffler, social critic, author of "Future Shock", "PowerShift" and
co-author of "War and Anti-War: Survival at the Dawn of the 21st Century", 
will speak on the emerging information age, the far reaching impacts of 
technology on the economy, and what new strategic vision America needs to 
adopt in order to survive in the new world order.  His talk will be on 
Wednesday, June 22, 1994 at 9:00 a.m.

Plenary: Dr. Timothy Leary, June 23
+++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++

Dr. Timothy Leary, a voice and influence for three generations of Americans, 
leading influencer in the futurist movement, will present an interactive 
session on how technology, such as multi-channeled television, CD-ROM and 
virtual reality, impacts individuals and society.  His presentation will 
take place Thursday, June 23 at 1:00 p.m.
