>From sameer@c2.org  Mon Jun 13 23:17:53 1994
Subject: The NEXUS-Berkeley is now on-line
To: nexus-berkeley@c2.org
Date: Mon, 13 Jun 1994 23:15:08 -0700 (PDT)
Pgp-Strong-Print: 3C AE E4 00 C2 6A 81 FF  49 4E EE 0C CD CD 1D 80

[Note: you haven't been subscribed to nexus-berkeley@c2.org without
your permission.. you're on a list that this message has been Bcc`d
to, if you are not subbed to nexus-berkeley@c2.org]

	-- Community ConneXion: The NEXUS-Berkeley is now on-line --

-- Please distribute widely.

	After many months of planning, thinking, frustration, and hard
work, Community ConneXion: The NEXUS-Berkeley is now on-line and ready
to begin its work.
	We've been thinking and dreaming about this for the past two
years. Finally we've made it into a reality.

	Community ConneXion (c2, c^2, or c-squared) has been founded
in order to build up a strong community in the internet both locally
and globally. We are linked into the worldwide NEXUS-Gaia movement
which is building up a worldwide community of like-minded
network-oriented individuals.

	We've realized that the internet is not about the protocols
nor the universities nor the corporations nor the politics which form
the basic infrastructure. All these things are merely the
facilitators, the parts which come together to produce the whole; the
internet is about people communicating and making connections with
each other-- forming the social infrastructure.
	We've appeared in order to facilitate these connections.

	We've setup shop here in the SF Bay Area and we will integrate
virtuality and reality. It is possible for virtual communities to
merge into, supplement, and sometimes even create "real"
flesh communities.

	In order to build up this community we've put some computers
on the internet and have started offering services. These are quality
services provided at a low cost, with an emphasis on community
involvement. We emphasize privacy because there can be no strong
community where people fear their neighbors. By allowing people to
selective reveal themselves, we make easier for them to break down the
walls of prejudice which come between people in social interactions.

	We're offering mailboxes, shell accounts, anonymous remailing
services, ftp space, domain names, mail exchanging, strong
psuedonymous identities, and more as time goes on.
	We're building up a barter-coupon system so that volunteers
who help our community can earn credits to use to buy more services
from our system or, as the NEXUS-Gaia project grows, from Nexi around
the world. The barter-coupon system is implemented using a secure and
private anonymous digital cash scheme.
	We're asking for help from people to build our community. It
can't be done with only a few people. Everyone involved can help out
to build the system. A community is a group effort. As we build the
community we improve our lives.

	For more information and to sign up, use your favorite
World-Wide-Web browser to look at http://www.c2.org or, if you don't
have access to a WWW browser, telnet to c2.org and login as
"guest". Most services are offered with an initial two week free trial
period.
	In order to subscribe to our mailing list, send the message
"subscribe nexus-berkeley" to majordomo@c2.org. (From a UNIX prompt:
"echo subscribe nexus-berkeley | mail majordomo@c2.org") If you have
any questions, send mail to info@c2.org.

-sameer
Community ConneXion: The NEXUS-Berkeley
Voice: 510-841-2014 (not yet active)
Pager: 510-321-1014
Email: info@c2.org

 last night i was in the perfect mood to go a party because i spent hours
geeking, and heard lots of things about about our scene. then i headed out
to a party that was free, outdoors, and just across town from me. wait...
it gets better. when i got to the party (around 5:00 or so) i was so
entranced by the 180 view of the horizon that it took me a while to notice
that there were no tanks hissing, no flyers/garbage on the ground.  we
were a group of about 50 or less, dancing, pumping out energy, feeling the
music inside...we got down! to me this party was a real treat because i
had never heard any of the dj's w/ the exception of scottie. the sound
system was perfect - living up to its name. the music flowed out of the
speakers which balanced the bass and treble very well. in short, the 
party was simple and beautiful.

	mother earth afterparty?...friends & family or basics?...  my
choice is the least expensive party (how can you beat $3?) well see you
all tonight :) :) :) (: (: (:  jason davis.

My computer sez that on Thu, 16 Jun 1994, Tamara Palmer wrote:

> I have a bit of a problem with you saying that there is no problem with you
> being open and frank about your illicit activities, but why then do you call
> yourself Starchild? How risky is it for you to say whatever you like on here
> with your identity hidden? I am not trying to attack you at all, I just find
> that a little curious and it's late and I am just trying to be devil's
> advocate here...

Dear Tamara, 

    That's a reasonable question, but actually the issue of my identity 
online being "hidden" by not using my legal name never occured to me.  I
guess I pretty much assume it would be easy enough in our hi-tech world
for anyone who really wants to track me down to do so.  I certainly don't
keep a bunch of phony passports and Swiss bank account numbers around the 
house (although I'd like to, if anyone has any extras - :) ) I go by 
Starchild off the net too, it's not just a computer handle, although I 
realize it sounds like one. 
    My philosophy is that it makes more sense to name yourself than to 
simply use a name chosen by your parents when they knew little about you, 
and when you might not even have much in common with them.  Of course 
changing your name is a hassle if your're used to being called one thing, 
and perhaps even more of a hassle for others to get used to, so I don't 
go by Starchild with my family and longtime friends who've known me by my 
birthname, unless they seem conducive to "Starchild."  And I don't 
usually go by Starchild on the job, again unless people seem receptive to 
it.  Unfortunately there are a lot of people in our society who are not 
yet enlightened enough to respect someone's choice of an unusual, or some 
would say "silly" name.
    The oddity & silliness of my name, however, are two of the things 
which endear it to me.  When people ask, I'll usually mention that it is 
a "ravename", or a name which grew out of my experience of going to 
raves, which is mostly true.  Although I used it sporadically online & 
such before I raved, I doubt I'd be calling myself Starchild now if I'd 
never attended a rave.  I've since met other people with "ravenames", and 
it always gives me a positive glow to meet them, as I recognize them as 
persons who, like myself, are in a small yet important way, poking at the 
fringes of what society considers "normal".
    Just like it's hard to take yourself too seriously when you're 
dressed like a Dr. Seuss character, it's hard to take yourself too 
seriously when you have a name like Starchild, or for that matter, R.U. 
Sirius, Wavy Gravy, DJ Fiasco, Captain Crunch, "Weird Al" Yankovic, "leg 
of eel", or many others I could name...
    I strongly suspect that if everyone took themselves a bit less 
seriously, the world might be a better place.

> Hug Your Waistline to the Bassline............................................
 
I like the sound of that, Tamara!  Hope I've answered your question...

> Tamara Palmer * trance@netcom.com * izzyzi5@mvs.oac.ucla.edu * 
> 
> .........................................................Women Respond to Bass

_______________________________________________________________________________
UPDATE:18 JUN 1994 

e  l  e     m  e  n  t: step 1


   OK folks, stuff is starting to roll.  We've received some submissions
for our free bi-monthly journal/magazine (net version and real physical
paper). Step 1 is due to come out nationally at the beginning of July, but
WE WANT MORE!!!!!!!!!! We want you to be a part of it!!!!! We know you're
out there....
   This is a sum up and update of what's up, with some technical specs. 
   If you read our first post you should know what kind of stuff we're
looking for but we will sum up here:


   *ele ment* is an attempt to bridge the gap between disciplines as far-
ranging as Detroit tekno, computer-aided design, John Waters movies,
skateboarding, and post-constructivist architecture (these are just a few
examples, among many).  It is a dialog between all the shit we're trying to
get together, from San Fran to London, all around and in between.  It's
about everything: what we're doing, what we're seeing, what we're thinking.
It's about the past, too, and how we can learn from it in the face of the
new millenium.
   Submissions can be ANYTHING legibly written or typed, on any subject, or
any theme.  It could be a review of your favorite record from 6 months ago
or 60 years ago. It could be a cool anthropology paper you wrote last
quarter.  It can be a poem, a photo, a CAD design, an editorial, a
diatribe, a letter, and so on.  
   
   All we ask is that you keep a couple of things in mind while considering
what to give us.  
   1) We plan to distribute nationally, in a selective manner such as
Camera Work in the 1900s or Emigre today (1000-1500 copies).  It's going to
look very nice!  We're using decent paper (slightly off-white stock) with
ring-binders (trust us, these look good and they are very distinctive).
This will be "coffee-table" material, or close to it, so we want quality
material that takes a world-wide perspective if possible.  
   For example, a friend of ours in Nashville wanted to write something
about his dance/rave (hate that word) scene.  We suggested he do something
like write it from the perspective of someone explaining the trials and
tribulations of trying to get that type of scene off the ground (as opposed
to just saying "Nashvlle sucks!").  We also scoured some women's studies
classes to get the female perspective known (there seems to be an unequal
balance of men on the electronic airwaves...). 
   Top ten lists should be avoided, unless they're informative.  If you can
make one like "my 10 faves of the last 6 months and WHY" that would be much
better than just a list with no descriptions or anything (notice that the
WHY is what we're more interested in).
   2) We want crazy amounts of diversity, in text and design.  It's your
opportunity to "design your own page."  Here's what's been decided on that
subject:
        
        -page size is 7.5 x 10 inches vertical.
        -radical is good (think Dada, Starn twins, or the new Creem...)
        -text or written entries that have not been pre-designed will be
distributed to other designers we know, or sometimes one of us (depends who
wants it!)
        -the only linking element besides maybe a "key" approach to the
reviews section (ie lump all reviews together and identify by a key code)
will be a small logo on the bottom of each page, unless your submission
specifies otherwise.
        -you have the option of telling us NOT to proofread your piece, if
your interest is in making anal grammarians cringe.
        -we'll print nearly all the submissions we get (unless they totally
ignore what we've said so far) so your chances of getting in with the
minimum of interference from us is like 90.25% or something. 
        
ADVERTISING:
We're trying to keep this minimal, to keep things clean and uncluttered,
but we will consider an ad if we can see it or talk to you first. This
being our 1st step we are offering dirt cheap prices, to cover our costs a
bit.
        
        -1/4 page is $15.00, 1/2 page is $30.00, full page is $60.00.
        -remember that the page size is 7.5 x 10 inches vertical.

THAT'S IT! Pretty simple recipe, actually. This mag is really made by YOU,
with us here to help corall things into a nice package. It may look
hodgey-podgey in the end, but that's OK--because, if you look at us and the
variety of our situations and influences, we look pretty hodgey-podgey
ourselves.



LAST LAST LAST DEADLINE is JUN 28 1994!!!!!!!!!!!

APOLOGY ON THE SHORT NOTICE, BUT...
We posted this on MWRaves a while ago, while forgetting everyone else.  If
you cannot get a submission to us on time send it anyway.  We'll put it in
step 1 if we can, or wait and put it in step 2 in September. 

It's up to YOU to make this happen.

hope to hear from you soon,


++
*the ele mental collective*

nbelcher@magnus.acs.ohio-state.edu
mcjones@magnus.acs.ohio-state.edu

[Note: you haven't been subscribed to nexus-berkeley@c2.org without
your permission.. you're on a list that this message has been Bcc`d
to, if you are not subbed to nexus-berkeley@c2.org]

	-- Community ConneXion: The NEXUS-Berkeley is now on-line --

-- Please distribute widely.

	After many months of planning, thinking, frustration, and hard
work, Community ConneXion: The NEXUS-Berkeley is now on-line and ready
to begin its work.
	We've been thinking and dreaming about this for the past two
years. Finally we've made it into a reality.

	Community ConneXion (c2, c^2, or c-squared) has been founded
in order to build up a strong community in the internet both locally
and globally. We are linked into the worldwide NEXUS-Gaia movement
which is building up a worldwide community of like-minded
network-oriented individuals.

	We've realized that the internet is not about the protocols
nor the universities nor the corporations nor the politics which form
the basic infrastructure. All these things are merely the
facilitators, the parts which come together to produce the whole; the
internet is about people communicating and making connections with
each other-- forming the social infrastructure.
	We've appeared in order to facilitate these connections.

	We've setup shop here in the SF Bay Area and we will integrate
virtuality and reality. It is possible for virtual communities to
merge into, supplement, and sometimes even create "real"
flesh communities.

	In order to build up this community we've put some computers
on the internet and have started offering services. These are quality
services provided at a low cost, with an emphasis on community
involvement. We emphasize privacy because there can be no strong
community where people fear their neighbors. By allowing people to
selective reveal themselves, we make easier for them to break down the
walls of prejudice which come between people in social interactions.

	We're offering mailboxes, shell accounts, anonymous remailing
services, ftp space, domain names, mail exchanging, strong
psuedonymous identities, and more as time goes on.
	We're building up a barter-coupon system so that volunteers
who help our community can earn credits to use to buy more services
from our system or, as the NEXUS-Gaia project grows, from Nexi around
the world. The barter-coupon system is implemented using a secure and
private anonymous digital cash scheme.
	We're asking for help from people to build our community. It
can't be done with only a few people. Everyone involved can help out
to build the system. A community is a group effort. As we build the
community we improve our lives.

	For more information and to sign up, use your favorite
World-Wide-Web browser to look at http://www.c2.org or, if you don't
have access to a WWW browser, telnet to c2.org and login as
"guest". Most services are offered with an initial two week free trial
period.
	In order to subscribe to our mailing list, send the message
"subscribe nexus-berkeley" to majordomo@c2.org. (From a UNIX prompt:
"echo subscribe nexus-berkeley | mail majordomo@c2.org") If you have
any questions, send mail to info@c2.org.

-sameer
Community ConneXion: The NEXUS-Berkeley
Voice: 510-841-2014 (not yet active)
Pager: 510-321-1014
Email: info@c2.org

Hello all!

Thanks for coming to Friends and Family and making it a HUGE 
RIP-ROARING SUCCESS!

The most amazing thing to me was how quickly the party got going. 
I'd encouraged people to get there at the beginning, and they did!  
The floor was well-occupied and dancing hard well before 11pm.  
Sometimes DJs don't like to go first because people often don't
straggle into parties until two hours after the announced start
time, but Friends and Family got up and going right away.

The people who run Komotion were GREAT and looked like they
were having fun, too.

A huge hand goes to the set-up crew who really made the space
special, from sweeping the floor to hanging lights and banners
to moving furniture and gear around.  When 10pm came around you
all had the place more than ready to open up for fun.

I'm sorry I left a bit after 4, but I had a house guest from
the UK who doesn't club or rave and I had to get back so I could
wake up Sunday to spend some time with him.

So once again *thanks* for the great music, the great setting,
the great dancing, the great party.  It took every single person
who came, from those dropping by to dance for a bit to those who 
stayed to the end and cleaned up to make the night as great as it 
was.  I met a number of sfravers whom I'd only known as email 
addresses or who have been lurking, that really made the night 
special for me.

Laura

P.S.  Next Up:  MetroVision goes HARDCORE (in both the Brooklyn and
UK sense of the word) -- Bryce, Lee An, and I got together and decided 
we are going to pull out our old breakbeat, gabber, Rotterdam, and German 
acid records and go forth on the industrial speedy noise tip.  If you've 
ever wondered . . . stay tuned for details.

 Good Hot Sweat At Friends and Family!

 I got to Club Kommotion at about 11:30PM , too late to hear Laura , so
I started the night with Ethan laying down some great music. 

 To get to the dancefloor , I walked through the "ambient hallway" where 
the ambient DJ turntables and equipment was set up. This was where Weird
Blinking Lights did their performance , and Ovid later did his feedback-
plaugued spoken piece with audio stage setting by M Normal. 

 The posted advice about wearing shorts was accurate - it was definitely
humid & hot! I wore my shorts under my pants , so it was easy to change
to a cooler mode. But it was so warm that I eventually took my checkered
Goofy t-shirt off my chest and pulled it back over my forehead , pharoah
style. It was the first time that I've done the bare-chested thing at a
party - there's much to recommend it!

 I don't think I'd go as far as one fellow - a slim guy with dirty-blond
shoulder length hair and short beard. The first I noticed him , I
thought he had a strange skin-tight set of leggings on with a dark
design at his crotch. The next glimpse , I realized that he was naked
- "skin-tight" indeed! Nobody I know seemd to be overly bothered by him
or harrasing him , I think he even got some encouraging remarks.

 Next to the DJ was a small table with florescent paints and a day-glo 
Slinky (tm). I had a lotta fun playing with that slinky ; by the way ,
later on in the evening , I saw a group of three huge football-linemen
types leaving the club , and one of them had the slinky. Since he seemed
to be about 3 times my body mass , I let him go by ...

 Lots of day-glo fun , with people playing with green glowing string, and
painting designs on themselves. Of course , there was soap bubble solution
as well ( thanks to Sean? ), which JUMP IN THE FIRE and Sean put to good
use later , when they found a good spot for the fan breezes to carry the
shiny bubbles over the crowd.
 
 The selection of DJs provided the dancers with a good variety of music,
techno and house. And all the DJ's doing it for free! Thanks! ( By the way,
did the benefit make enough money for the club ? ).

 Mucho SFRavers there : Maui , good to see that you were able to make it!
Welcome back Susie ( how long were you gone? ).Will Penna brought more
rave newbies from Santa Cruz - how did they like it? Scott N. - it was
kind of dim there - that was Loren with you , wasn't it? The only SFRaver
that I didn't notice there was Capt'n Crunch (?). Hello to everybody else I
didn't mention.

 This Friends and Family party reminded me of my third rave - Vortex ,
that was in a small warehouse outside of San Francisco. They both had
good vibes aplenty, a humble setting, and a hot, humid atmosphere. I'm
looking foreward to more of 'em!

	Larry Ching/larryc@netcom.com

Greetings, Ravers!

I had the most amazingly good time and friends and family--it was such a 
delight to see so many people having such a good time!  i had been working
lots of overtime in orange county for a client for most of the week prior,
and drove back on saturday.  i was really quite tired, but committed to
setting up the sound in the ambient hallway.  after helping set up and 
whatnot, i lay down on a couch in the lounge around 10ish.  i remember 
hearing a bit of scuffling and what not.  i got up around 10:20 or so,
and wandered into the dance room and saw quite a few people there already.
i was really very surprised to see so many people dancing so soon--although
i had said on the voice mail that we were to start at "a real 10 o'clock",
so many parties don't seem to take off until midnight, or even 2AM.  effandeff
was going full tilt, it seemed, right from the start....and stayed going full
blast until almost 6AM!

wowzee!  this was one of the most amazingly good times i've had in a long
while...everybody's energy just carried me through the night.  i just woke
up (it's about 2:30AM on monday morning) from an extended sleep...that's
how tired my body was.  komotion is a great space.  i heard from ethan that
komotion made what they needed, and more! at the door.  thanks again to
everyone who contributed financially to komotion's benefit...they really
appreciated it, and i'm sure they'd thank you all personally.  i loved the
entire setup.

for me, i knew we had gone over the top when:  i was fiddling with Sound
Vision during ethan's set.  i heard something hit the floor, and looked 
over to see what it was....i was sitting on the floor (pre-condensation),
and only glanced, but it was someone's clothes.  i saw a bare body, and
KNEW that we had achieved a real comfort zone that i've *never* experienced
at a house party in san francisco.  i've seen it happen at faery parties,
but never at "generic" parties.  i was really happy that everyone was
so comfortable (and, hot!) that this was ok.

i loved the lasers, and donovan's light show, and the art work, and all the
DJ sets, and all the folks who came by to dance and hang out with us.  i 
really look forward to more good times with you all!  i really wish that i
had had more energy and time to hang out with you all, and i'm looking
to the next one so i can do that.  thanks, everyone, for taking another
SFR party over the top!
-- 
Bryce Ryan ------- AMBIANCE ----------- brycer@crl.com-----

Here's a message I'm relaying from Preston (of Groove Kitchen fame):

On July 16th the Groove Kitchen Family and friends will be holding a
hoedown in Portland, Oregon.  On our way up North we will be heading to
Eugene on the weekend of July 8th, 9th and 10th to partake in the
festivities at the Oregon Country Fair.  The fair is located in Veneta,
which is 13 miles West of Eugene.  This will be their 25th year of getting
together and offering the best in arts, crafts, and grubbin' food,
surrounded by music.  If this interests you please feel free to join us. 
This years fair is shaping up to be well attended, so please think and call
ahead.  The Oregon Country Fair does have an admission fee, for details and
advance ticket sales please call 503.343.6554.  Places to stay are hard to
come by during the fair weekend, so here's a small list of motels and

It was crazy, it was wild, it was out of control! This was no house
party, this was a RAVE!

People showed up early, and kept the place packed with about 200
people all night long. The music was outstanding. Tomatsu was
especially on, relentlessly making me dance even though I wanted to
sit down :).

Here's what $3 bought you:

Great dance and ambient DJs, live music, toys, banners, lasers,
visuals, two bathrooms, a party that started 1/2 hour EARLY, a
beautiful altar with free fruit, ins-&-outs, friendly doorpeople, free
water, body paint, the storm-O-bubbles (tm), lots of fans (we told you
it'd be hot), no police, and a smooth running crazy wild fun party all
night long.

And not only did the party pay for itself, it made enough money to
save the space.

Many thanks to everyone who made this party happen. It was a truly
cooperative effort, everyone had a part in it.

We'd just finished dropping off the sound system afterwards, and I
said to Ethan:

"You know, you can't buy [a vibe] like that."

He said, "And you can't sell it either. You can only give it away."

:)

Sean

I must say they delivered beyond expectations!  Great scene, great
weather Saturday and Sunday after we got drenched during the show
on Friday.  I don't think the sound system from Seattle ever showed
up, and I didn't bring my records anyway due to a mixup on my ride
down (I ended up taking the bus from Portland at 5 am Friday morning!).
And the Dead delivered one of their longest and best shows in years
yesterday!  We even had a rainbow directly overhead during the show --
a friend of mine tells me that's called a 'sundog' -- never even heard
of such a thing before . . .

I'm very pleased to hear how well things went at Kommotion.  This is the
kind of event that's going to head us into new directions  . . . 
props to EVERYONE for doing it!!

see you in the future

phred

Good Morning SFR! 

(he, he; just call me rumplestilskin).

WOW! What a party :) This one exceeded my wildest dreams; it was, I think,
everything we wanted it to be, and then some...

You know, I often say to people, "Thanks, we couldn't have done it without
you" and I think that we're so used to hearing this phrase that it's
meaning goes right by us. So I want to pay special attention to that phrase
now. We could not have done it without *you*: the people that showed up at
6pm, spent the next *4* hours setting up, danced all night and then helped
us clean up and take the gear home; everyone that brought decorations and
alters and helped make the space beautiful; everyone that came and danced
and smiled and helped create the *vibe*, all the djs and musicians,
speakers, thinkers, dreamers, and nude guys ;-) You *all* helped make this
a really special night that will bring a smile to my face and warm glow to
my soul as long as I live. Good job.

I also want to extend special thanks to all the folks at Komotion.
Unfortunately, one of the things that commerializes our scene is the fact
that spaces cost money (and big spaces cost big money). From the get go
Komotion was willing to do this party on a very low cost, no-cash-up-front,
whatever-happens-is-cool basis. This kind of attitude, this vibe is what it
takes to do Saturday night parties with all the trimmings for $3. However,
what I treasure most about Komotion's attitude is that it contains
something I place special value on: trust. The real bonus is that we lived
up to the trust they placed in us. We gave them an awesome demonstration of
just how good a job, we as a community can do and, more importantly, what,
exactly, the acid house vibe is all about. And guess what: They loved it!
Without a doubt they had as good a time as we did and, not surprisingly,
they want to do it again :)

Music was killer all night long. Laura already a good vibe goin when I took
the decks and, despite spending 5-10 minutes in the twilight zone (weird) I
had a pretty good time. Lee pulled off the best and longest mix into Circus
Bells I've ever heard and generally cooked us with nice, hard, acidic,
tribal trance. Alex spent a little longer in the twilight zone than I did
but soon settled down and and as usual unleashed the kind of music you'll
be hard pressed to find anywhere else in SF. Having not heard Tamotsu in 6
months I have to confess to being *blown away*; Tamostsu, you shred! I hope
you get the exposure you deserve! Spun had a hard time escaping world
groove and so arrived at us a bit (too) late, which, all in all, was okay
as things were starting to wind down at that point anyway. Not to worry,
he'll be back. Excellent visuals by donovan who, by the way, is an
amazingly cool dude. I really look forward to working with him some more in
the future; his heart's definitely in the right place.

One final note: one of the things that made me *really* happy was that, by
and large, I think the vast majority of the 200-250 people that came to
this party were list (sfr) folks. I met tons of people from the net that I
never even knew existed. Nice folks too! SFR RULES!  ;-)

lots of love
ethan

 ethan miller                     nrg                            pgp me

                (: positive energy can save the world :)
               __________________________________________

Weekend Rave report
===================
  
  I can't believe I missed F&F,   I'll never forgive myself for
missing this event,  as I had fully intended to make a showing,
but Craig wanted me to hemp him with the technical end of the 
video.

  This Saturday,  I had attended "Cool World" at the Cow Palace,
where my friend Craig Larson did the video,  so I was spared from
having to pay the exhorbenent $25 admission fee.    Instead,  I
had an "All Access" badge that got be backstage,  and also access
to a free food buffet,  ins-and-out's and other perks.

  The promoters had mentioned there was to be an orbitron and
gravitron,  but (sigh!) these "rides" never showed up.   Nothing
love better,  than to twerl around on an orbitron.

Other than that,  "Dee Lite" put on an awsome show when they went 
on stage around 5 am or so.

   The main arena was mostly hip hop towards the end,   with Techno
DJ'ing between the live music acts.     

   There were 3 areas,   one a hip hop/ Acid Jazz area on one side of
main arena,  the other was "house" on the other side,   and then the main 
arena,  which had a ferris wheel and tilt-a-whirl with waiting times
of about an hour for each of the rides.

   The "House" section was killer,  but the very large room didn't do
the sound much justice,  as the echoing effect made for a somewhat 
muddy sound.   The space (Cow Palace) was killer,  with lots of room,
little or no smoking (Actually there was no smoking,  but few people
obeyed it).

   As usual,  I went insane in the house section,   but the first few
DJ's failed to keep my interest for long,   then at about 5 am,  I saw
Garth coming down the ramp in the backstage area,  and I knew that
my wants for good continious beats would soon get answered.

   I had fully intended to leave Cool World and head over to Friends
and Family,   but my partner Aaron had the keys to the car,  and
couldn't be found (sigh!) so I got bored around 3 am and couldn't
get over there.     I heard that F&F was THE place to be,  from reports
I've gotten from Robert,  who I met the following morning at the End
Up.

   After the Cool World,  we headed down to the Mission area for a big
breakfast,   Aaron and my other friend Mike,  wanted to hang out in the
Castro,   while I met and visited another friend before eventually
heading over to the End up.    My stay was short,   as this is Gay 
Pride weekend and the Gay parade was to start soon,  so I head over to
the festival area and hung out till the parade started.

   The parade was of course totally insane (As only San Francisco can
provide.    Very entertaining,  the costumes were totally out of this
world,  and we were blessed with wonderful warm weather (Unusual for
this time of year).   I found a great spot to view the parade,  and
chilled out,  until I got restless and headed up Market street.

   After the parade, we headed ofer to the festival area,  and lo
and behold,  the sound of house music was drawing me towads it,  and
I wound up dancing my ass off until 6 pm.    I thought most of the
DJ's SUX bigtime,  as few could keep up a good beat for long.   As
frequent announcements were made,  chastizing those folks for sitting
on the speakers and hanging out to near the DJ area.    As usual,
it was super crowded,  but I did manage to find enough room to dance
and had a great time.

   My only regret was that I missed F&F,  as I had fully intended to
make an appearance.

   So,  for those wanting to know about "Cool World",  you didn't miss
anything good,  as I would say it was mediocre (At best) and NOT worth
the $25 (Plus $6 for parking),  but I know you all knew that anyway.

CC

I agree with everything good that's been said about this party. d;-)  Lotsa 
visuals, props, smiles, people - the communal effort was obvious making the 
space as fun and stimulating as any indoor venue I can remember being in.  
The fans, free water, ins & outs, and no smoking policy made the heat quite 
tolerable.  We even found the slippery wet concrete fun to dance on.
  
The music:

Family obligations limited our attendance to the 2:30 - 5:30 slot, but
I was very impressed with the DJing.  It was the first time I heard
Tomatsu spin, and he *really* kicked making it difficult for us to leave. 
 
The ambient DJs had to battle with the main room, which was too bad, 
because M Normal, our ambient queen, gave us a truly beautiful set.  I 
really like her style of beatless mixing, music you can really float away 
and bliss out with.  I thought that her selection for Ovid's talk was 
perfect, even inspired.  I'm gonna have to start bugging her to make me 
a tape. 

The "talk":

The ambient hallway may not have been the most ideal venue for Ovid's 
spoken work performance, but I thought that this still ended up being 
a very special event.  M spun some eeringly beautiful space music while
red laser blobs streaked over Ovid's head like fiery comets.  The nearby
dance room entrance flared the energy of new born stars at us and 
occasional humans walked by like rocky asteroids drifting through 
our hallway region of the galaxy.  And in the midst of this swirling
turmoil/harmony of sound, light and motion, Ovid spoke to us of yourneys 
to Infinity, of the place between experience and understanding... he was 
a vortex of consciousness amidst a pulsating and chaotically organized 
Cosmos.  To me, this represented what I have always felt the ultimate 
transcendental experience should be about: getting to a "place" where 
there is total synergy between Mind and Universe.

Even when it was difficult to hear everything Ovid said, I would catch 
phrases of a metaphysical nature that would triggered various esoteric 
themes existing at the limits and core of our minds and reality.  More than 
a poetry reading or a lecture - it was a word performance based on deep 
scientific and spiritual understandings.  As far as reality explorations go, 
Ovid's excursion had much more meaning for me (even when I could only make 
out peices of it) than Terrance Mckenna's psychedelic court jestering.

Thanks Ovid, and thank you Ethan for enthusiastically embracing the whole 
idea of this from the very start.  Isn't raving cool - silly, fun, sensory,
decadent, technological, scientific, artistic, social, spiritual... pick 
one, or pick 'em all.
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
Lee Fogel/\/\/\/\/\eVerything/\Is/\possiBlE/\/\/\/\/\lxfogel@srv.pacbell.com

What a beautiful thing when reality overwhelms expectations.  Due
to family obligations we arrived a little late after taking a nap,
in time to see Ovid give his talk with M Normal doing a terrific
job setting a truely wonderful mood.  Too bad it was a little
hard to hear, but I know that there was enthusiasm for this type
of performance and i'm sure that Ovid will do it again in the future.  

As soon as we walked into the club we were struck by the vibe - WOW!
so many smiling faces and pure joy.  I truly felt that we were all
in this together, feeding off of everyone's infectious good feeling.
It was also so sweet to see so many SFR's in one place; its been a 
long time since i've seen so much community.  We arrived too late to
meet the naked guy, which, when i read about it, thought it was
absolutely hilarious (what a scene this is).

Unfortunately, the only DJ we got to see was Tomatsu; he was
spectacular.  I have never heard him spin before and truly hope that
i get to see him again soon.  While true, it was very hot in the
large room, i never felt uncomfortable...the fans and the fact that
everyone adhered to the no smoking rule as well as plenty of free water 
was probably why.

Lastly, my biggest congratulations to Ethan and to Bryce.  Two people
who continue to embrace the concept and hope of continuation.  They
have endured dispite some disappointments and a whole lot of hard work. 
Not for recognition or money, but for their devotion to the scene.
I love you guys.  

janie

  OFFICE MEMO          F&F                                    Date:6/20/94

Wow!

     Even though I was totally beat from running around all day, I managed to
dance through most of Laura's set and a little into Ethan's.  After that I
chilled with my fiance on the risors and twitched and watched the crowd go off.
 NO SMOKING!  This was a big plus in my book because it allowed me to breath
and enjoy the party without having to choke.  The heat was definitely in the
house, but I like what it adds to the vibe.  Bryce & Ethan, the sound was
PERFECT 8*)  I have been to few clubs were the sound is EQed as well and sounds
so tasty *Long live the Bass*.  Even on the turntables, where sound can be a
nightmare, it felt like my head was surfing on a standing wave of music 8*)  It
was great to have so many people there right from the start.  It made the party
start at the begining, imagine that ;)  The ambient room was too cool, next
time there should be more room so that more people can enjoy dream land at the
same time!  
     Bathrooms, soap, free cold water, friendly workers, no goons, very
friendly vibe(let's hear it for smiles), big cool fans, dayglow paint(which was
cool to spin with on my hands), glow sticks, flourecent slinky(Go Larry!!),
Lasers, ambient and dance Djs KICKED!!!  
     I had a great time and can't wait for the next SFR event.  I had some
non-SFR friends drop by who really enjoyed themselves.  Everybody give yourself
a hand!!!

Peace & Strength 'till we Trance again !              Tamotsu


Next time I'm raving naked 8*)

Family and Friends--

That's what we all were Saturday night at Klub Kommotion,
thanks to a lot of loving work--and working love--that a
lot of people put in. I cannot add to the kudos; the names
are a litany of the known and the unknown: Laura, Brian,
naked guy, Greg the glopainter and his friend Scott who
were newbies that I had fun guiding around a bit, Alan and
Jim who were newbies I brought for their first rave, Larry,
RSN8, M and ovid who took us on a trip where music and meta-
physics and subatomics and spirituality intersect, Ethan, Bryce, 
Tomatsu, Lee, Alex and forgive me for whoever I don't mention!

teacher Robert (who's only existed in cyberspace for me so far)
and a new friend, met recently in the ether on the occasion of
flaming some rather provocative stuff I had to say last week!

Subject: Troy Finds San Francisco
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Date: Mon, 20 Jun 1994 20:18:03 -0700 (PDT)
Cc: socal-raves@UCSD.EDU

What?  You mean it was right up the 101 the whole time?
Actually, I found the heart and soul of San Francisco, what the San 
Francisco people always talk about when they compare it to
Los Angeles.

I'm posting this to SFraves and So-Cal raves, because while in
LA I never really knew what made the SF scene so great, I didn't
really understand why everyone was moving up there.

Until Saturday night.

I went to both Friends and Family (put on by SFravers) and Basics.
First, let me say that I had agreat time at F&F.  I want to thank
the people who put it together.  For 3 dollars they provided a 
secure location, 2 good sound systems, lights, DJ's, and a vibe!
Many times I am lucky to get one of those things for 15 dollar.
A special "Hi!" to everyone I met there.  

Now, I don't want my opinion of Basics to undermine F&F, because
they were really two altogether different events, both special
in their own right.

Basics was simply the best even I have ever been to.  Basics seemed
to have a format, a program if you will.  It was not like a typical 
club where people come and go throughout the night.  Basics was
more like a service.  It had three distinct parts.  

Pat 1:  When I arrived I was a bit surprised that more people were 
not dancing.  But looking around I saw most of the people talking,
socializing, meeting up with friends and meeting new people.  
There seemed to be a feeling o knowing, of anticipation, maybe
the way a family might act before a wedding.  A feeling that everyone was about
to have a really good experience.  The music at
this point was a faster, progressive house.  

Part 2:  Large baners with fluorescent paint were lit up by many
blacklights up until this point.  At about 2:15am, when most people
had started dancing, the blacklights went out, the club fell into
darkness, and a large cheer came from the crod.  Something was
happening.  The music changed.  I had heard this music a few times
before.  Nothing terribly different, just another step in the ever-
evolving realm of progressive dance tracks.  It was a bit darker,
trancier, almost pagan, but, amazingly, it retained funk and house
elements.  I guess this is "The San Francisco Sound", whatever
that means.  But this was, above all else, dance music.  This was
music that got me moving unlike anythig else I have really
heard.  My mind let go and my body took over.  
I'm not going to try and explain how I felt.  I thought how I would
explain this in a "xxxxxx-raves" post.  The one comment that
came to mind that seemed realy appropriate was "dancing
with God".  I was in a state where I could not think of anything
that could possibly make this experience better.  A feeling that
everything within me and around me was in perfect balance.
I was not he only one.  The vibe around
me was unlike anything I have ever experienced, so much so that
the term "vibe" was totally redefined for me.  I could ramble on for
a long time about how I felt for the next 3 hours, but it is on of 
those things that you have to experience to really understand.

Part 3:  At around 4:45 the black-lights went back on, the DJ
poured on the House.  House spun just like I, personally, love it.
It was the perfect music to ollow up what we had gone through.
The one word to describe the atmosphere was "celebration".  We
left our euphoric trances to share and dance with each other.
A more perfect sense of acceptance and co-existance I have
never flt.  We had experienced true joy for ourselves, and now it
was time to share it with the people around us.  Morning came,
and the club was over.

There is a either a new generation of raves ("Raves:TNG"?), or the
evolution has passed over Southern California.  Either way, there
is something happening out there, up here, that is wonderful.
I hope to see many so-cal friends visit up here soon!

-troy

hi.

i suppose i'm one of the many referred to as "lurkers"..  but i did 
manage to make it out to friends and family, and i must say i thought it 
was incredible.

the music was fantastic and the crowd was so energized ...  i couldn't 
help but smile.  it seemed everyone else couldn't help but smile either. :)  
it was a bit hot at first, but it didn't take us long to forget about the 
heat and we spent the next few hours dancing our bums off.  it was the 
type of situation where my brain keeps telling me i'm tired but my body has 
control and  won't stop..  i felt so wonderfully comfortable and content...

never got around to meeting any list folk..  maybe next time (which i 
hope isn't too far off)

just wanted to say i had a great time all around.  appreciated all the 
smiles and general friendliness.  :)

thanks to all..  really, thanks so much for providing such a great and 
satisfying party.


 - seth

Troy:  

Feels good to know that other people feel as I do, that the rave scene 
is, not better than the rest, but has an extremely healthy vibe.  And a 
large part of what makes the scene here so healthy is the contribution 
from the people that put on the Basics parties.  

Every time I go to Basics I see more and more people that I have at one 
time or another met there.  I call it a "rave family" or "Basics Family", 
or whatever.  The point is the same people go there, so it is not only a 
rave, it has become over the past 2 years a gathering of friends.  

I'm glad that you had fun up here.  I have never been personally to a 
s-cal rave, so I can't give my opinion on how the vibe is there--but the 
vibe is alive here, and what I ask of people is to take that positive 
energy with them and spread the word.  

dj fog

SF Guardian, 6/8/94, p.16  (Nude Beaches '94 article)

	At Santa Cruz's Boony Doon, volunteers are picking up trash
	rather than planting seeds.  Since it began five years ago, 
	this annual cleanup, led by the South Bay Naturists, has been 
	nothing short of miraculous.  In previous years the patrol 
	has hauled about a ton of bottles and other trash from the 
	outskirts of the sandy cove.  "Last year we found just 500 
	pounds," says Richard Pasco, head of the San Jose-based 
	naturists group.  This season, the battle to transform the 
	site continues.  If you'd like to help during a daylong 
	cleanup on Sept. 17, contact SBN [South Bay Naturists]...

Two points:
  According to this article, Bonny Doon has been _cleaner_ since 
  raves started happening there!  This certainly doesn't directly 
  imply that all events there leave the site "cleaner than when 
  we got there", but it does argue that this is _not_ a case of a 
  pristine site trashed by massive raves.

  i recall a thread a few months ago about the possibility of 
  having a clean-up day down there.  Were plans ever finalized? 
  Perhaps those interested might want to join this cleanup in 
  September... (a clothing optional trash pickup -- interesting 
  concept :)
		
						
							gregg

That guy from So-Cal reminded me of a party where I had one of those 
godly experiences, last year at the 4th of Jul "Let Freedom Rave" in 
Livermore at a dirt racetrack.  This was a party that almost ended right 
in front of our eyes, but the ravers stopped that from happening.  

First of all, what reminded me of what Troy said about the music was a set
at the Let Freedom Rave party last year.  I believe the lights either
dimmed or went out, and there was this incredible "space-techno" (I create
a new musical genre almost daily) that was just incredible.  I think it
was Spun spinning, but I am not sure.  Anyway, I think that happened about
1:00 or so. 

Then, about 2:15 am, people began pointing up in the hill next to the 
party.  People had been lighting fireworks all night, and one of them got 
into the dry grass and started the hill on fire.  It started really fast, 
and before anyone knew it, the fire was going.  

People began running up there to try to put the fire out.  Some people 
kicked dirt on it, others used buckets or bottles of water that were at 
the front.  The fire spread to this big tree, and I thought that it was 
over then.  The music had stopped by this time and Martin told  
people to get off the hill over the pa.  

However, there were already tons of people on the hill.  They soon had the
tree problem out of the way.  The rest of us sat and watched in suspense,
and when the tree stopped burning, the entire crowd cheered with complete
ecstatic joy.  Martin got on the pa and said "Let's put the fire out
together" so we could start the party again.  About 10 minutes later, the
music started again, and that changed the entire mood of the party. 

When the sun came up, some of us climbed on the hill to watch the party 
from up there and reflect on the night.

Ken recently asked me about Streetlight Records on Bascom Ave. in San
Jose -

> Interestingly, the last good vinyl store in the South Bay Area was in
> the same area - maybe even on the same block < as Outer Rhythm Records >
> - it might even still be
> there, called Streetlight Records.  I haven't been there in about three
> years, but back then they had tons of vinyl.
> 
> Any idea if it is still there?  
> respect,
> 
>     Ken
> 
> 
 Yes and no - the store still exists , but it's moved down to a huger 
store next to Quement Electronics , past HW280 and the hospital , across
the street from World of Fantasy comics. Bascom Ave is getting to be this 
strange kind of "auto row" of prerecorded music - Outer Rhthym at one end , 
then Rowe's Rare Records , then Streetlight , and finally Tower Records in
Campbell.

 Streetlight has about 24" of techno/ambient CDs - they used to have a
seperate techno section , but they discontinued the seperate section
some months ago ( their hearts were never into techno , I guess - the
divider marking the Techno 12" had this written on it " This is the 
TECHNO section - it's just a flash in the pan , anyway" ). Too bad -
they used to have all the Twitch remix 12".

	Larry Ching/larryc@netcom.com

Two weekend party reviews:
(my psuedo-vacation of not working on weekends continues)

Friday I got into 1015 Folsom for free around 12:30.  I had never been.
It is a bit of a zoo.  The basement is House.  There is a chill no roof
with heaters room that I checked out just before they closed it - it was
suitably chilly ;) 

My impression is that this space has been bagged on alot on this list.
I thought it was great.  A bar with lots of ice water, AC into a little 
screened off area that stayed cooler.  The screen had visual stuff.
There was a harsh black light but plenty of places to look away and it
is fairly key to be able to turn into a bright light at an appropriate 
time.  There were enough people to keep things On and have space to
move.

The crowd worked me!  I was inspired.  Beautiful people.  
Dressed to go OUT.  I was on this decadent disco head trip.
Each moment was a picture - frozen - 
the *Fabulous* contorted into insane boogie
manuevers - droplets of sweat winging through the air -
Brazilian jet setters and international soccer stars -
I got off hard

To compare it to my (quite) limited party experiences I would say 
it was closest to a Toon Town - at least people wise.  
I guess this makes it old school.
DJ's Taj and Thomas.  
How does it go?
Thomas is the shit!

This is not a weekly (I think) but it will be
later in the summer ..??

Saturday I went to F&F - $3 was nice as were the ins and outs
The chill room was loud.  The chill-chill room had bathroom traffic.
The main room was hot as hell at least early in the night.
The music just didn't do me right (no flames please).  
I stuck around until Spun came on (I think).
Bong Bong Bong come-dance-to-me house.
I was tired so I left.
I had on baggy blue jeans and a tshirt.  Didn't meet any sfravers
but I did meet some nice folks from Pacifica.  Also (pet peeve coming)
some guy asked me Several Times to sell him drugs.  
After one "sorry no - good luck though" 
what is up with asking me again?
This only seems to happen to me
at places that allow under 21
I must look like a shady character ... ;);) 

Dave

Susie et al--

We all know al, but "et" doesn't mean...well,
it means "and" and "al" is short for *alii*
and means "others," natch?

Well, anyways, Susie named it right: things go in seven
year cycles and it was 1966, the year before the "summer
of love," that morpho genetic fields built up in the
whole SF scene (not just the Haight-Ashbury) to make
that scene then.

Well, this is now, but count 'em!  I was at my big
turning point entheogenic opening by 1966 when I was
28 and when I hit 56 the next phase hit me.  Ever see
that Brit documentary "28+," then it was "35+," etc.?
28 is when most of us transit to "adulthood," and 56?
Well, 1994 has the portent of 1966....

Susie  :) it was good chatting with you, too, at F&F2!
No, I *won't* say "partyon"!

Received: by SLACVM (Mailer R2.08 R208004) id 8124;
          Tue, 21 Jun 94 18:11:17 PST
Date: Tue, 21 Jun 1994   18:02 -0800 (PST)
From: JACOB%SLACVM.BITNET@Forsythe.Stanford.EDU
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: week report, seattle article (long)
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

hi folx,
really enjoyed friends and family. got there around 1 am and felt a really
good vibe in the whole place. i really liked the musick being spun in the
dance room. the ambient room was cool too, tho' a bit busy with  people
going back an forth. saw quite a few people, even some folx who came to their
first  rave. the spoken visualisation went pretty well, tho' there were some
technical problems at times with feed-back.
earlier last week i was in seattle and got a bit of taste of the nw scene.
i must say that i was staying at a place near u of w and was not that mobile,
so i got to go to the underground ONLY. 1 out of 3 ain't bad in baseball,
bit not so good in dancing . the acid house night on wed.'s was good, but the
'alternative industrial' night on tue. and the fri. were so so only.
hope there are more vibey place, since at the undgnd people were not that
friendly. i did pick up some mags up there, including a neat hip-hop
magazine, THE FLAVOR, which had a neat article i want to share with you all
about hip-hop, jeru and such:
" i express myself freely or i just won't do it...if something's on my mind,
i say it ten times out of ten."
i hear lots of talk about the uprising of the black race and the means by
which we  plan  to take back our freedom. and all i can say is , i hope
motherfuckers don't think this is going to be a shoot'em up free-for-all,
going around killing innocent people and reacting to our pain and confusion
like uncontrolled animals. hell yeah, you'll scare the white politicians;
you'll scare them so much with out violent, uncontrolled, unpremeditated
revolution that they will drop a bomb on our black asses so fast there will
be just craters where ghettos were. don't you see all this gun shit is not
the way. they gave them to us so we would act up and when everyone asks,
"why did they bomb the black people?" they will tell them we got out of hand,
and they did it to protect themselves and their country, and americans  will
nod in pacified agreement and go back to sleep.
  we as black people don't know enough about ourselves to be talking of an
 uprising. we embarrass ourselves too much everyday, from kids killing each
other in the streets for nothing for a substance they must rush to sell other
black people as if it were healing them. but all crack gas done us stagnate
the growth of our culture, and destroy our families. and the sorry-ass r&b
and rap has made a self-mockery of our real music such as jazz, funk, soul,
reggae and hip-hop that we execute with such inexperience that it's as if
we stole the music from them and don't understand what it means or where it
comes from. this is sad because they have stolen our heritage and will gladly
sell us a piece of it for the price of our soul and dignity. we then turn
this regurgitated soul against each other and these shallow compositions of
confusions have become anthems for black people. millions of balck people have
been tricked into throwing away themselves, but in so many different ways all
they have to do is sit back and watch in suspended relief until the last black
person drops.
  for this very reason the so-called revolution must be a mental one, and must
be constructed of such power and love for each other that we cannot fail and
will reclaim our right to live on this planet like we belong here. jeru is
one brother who has already made steps in the direction of building his
intellect into a protective force-field he can use to protect himself and
others who chose to listen. but the year is 1994 and there isn't much time left
and it seems that true hip-hop has stepped up to take its place in the battle
against ignorance, but must fight ignorance within its own genre to survive.
when i asked jeru how he felt his new album, "the sun rises in the east,"
would stand against the wall of ignorance and chaos that has been erected to
keep us out, he said "it's gonna stand in its own spot.. amongst all that.
everything has got its own place and time and so does my music. so it really
doesn't matter, there really is no chaos because chaos is just a different
aspect of order."
  that makes a lot of sense, but at the same time people find it frightening
to even go outside, and it's not even a night thing anymore. you could get
took out in broad daylight, which is truly disgusting because a lot of older
people and children can't go outside. some of us have actually adapted in a
chilling disposal of emotions, except fear that we try to disguise as anger
among other things.
  "fuck that, fuck being scared of my people," said jeru."it's like the time
for that is over..., being scared of one another and all that. there ain't
really shit to be scared of," professed jeru. "it shouldn't be your brother
bustin' you in the head for something like a jacket of something. motherfuckers
make you dead for something already dead."
   it's very confusing to me, though, 'cause it seemed like between the years
1988 through 1991 brothers were rhyming about mental shit, but were led
astray. but why ?
   "it's got to do with the masses. it got too large. so the ignorant are
going to embrace ignorance. it's like a wise man embraces intelligence," jeru
said, commenting on the sudden disappearance of the intellectually-strengthened
balck minds that we so desperately need to lead us out of this confusion and
into the righteous domain of constant growth and enlightenment that we have
been removed so far from. that without our true, original way of existence
that we have been brought here brainwashed. therefore without our supernatural
mental capabilities we have been rendered defenseless, and have seemingly no
other choice  but to flip. like when jeru says, "homicide central, east
new york, where the manic-depressive-psycho-murderers stalk " in he song
  "come clean. " now think about that, "manic-depressive-psycho-murderers,"
that could be any of us. when i asked jeru if he thought that would grab
people's attention, he knew it had to. he said why. "in fact that could be
some dude fed up with work or whatever, and he's gotta feed his family, so
he needs to do what he's gotta do. brothers is just fed up with being
niggas instead of men or gods."
   if this is the case, then we need to come together, not to fight a physical
war, so they can wipe our bodies from the planet with such amazing ease that
it won't matter now many we bring, but through our love for each other, our
culture, and most important, the mental and spiritual elevation we experience
and can share with each other through our music. until then, we will suffer
for lifetimes into eternity and the revolutions we speak of will be nothing
more than occasional fits thrown by black people who are fed, but not enough
to feed our minds souls, and hearts with the beauty that lies within ourselves
and each other.
                                       THE FLAVOR

take care/shalom
ovid

from my friend Fen . . . 

>From fen@imagine.comedia.com Tue Jun 21 12:46:45 1994
Subject: Summer Solstice!

	Today as we celebrate the longest day of the year,
	let all that we long for and all that we work for
	ripen and feed us with the fruits of our labors.

	Reflect upon the beautiful Rose, complete with
	blossom and with thorn, fragrance and blood:
	As we reap that which we have sowed, we must also
	grow to accept the passing of the Sun, as the Day
	again begins to give way to the dark of Night.

	May you on this day of Light see with clear Sight.


With wishes for your Health and Happiness, Peace and Prosperity,
Fen

On Tue, 21 Jun 1994 JACOB%SLACVM.BITNET@forsythe.stanford.edu wrote:

> earlier last week i was in seattle and got a bit of taste of the nw scene.
> i must say that i was staying at a place near u of w and was not that mobile,
> so i got to go to the underground ONLY. 1 out of 3 ain't bad in baseball,
> bit not so good in dancing . the acid house night on wed.'s was good, but the
> 'alternative industrial' night on tue. and the fri. were so so only.
> hope there are more vibey place, since at the undgnd people were not that
> friendly. i did pick up some mags up there, including a neat hip-hop
> magazine, THE FLAVOR, which had a neat article i want to share with you all
> about hip-hop, jeru and such:
Well, compared to everything else that goes on here in Seattle, such as 
the UFO/ATOI parties, the Choc-Lit factory events, Mind Body and Soul and 
whatnot, the Underground is crap crap crap.  Basically it's a teen dance 
club not unlike another in town called The Oz.  Nothing "vibey" about it 
whatsoever.  Anyway, enough bitching.  It's a shame you couldn't make it 
out to Starseed, which was held in a Port Authority park by the water 
(framed by these enormous loading cranes) and came to completion with 
*the blessing of the authorities*... Michael Manahan, Dervish, Ryan, and 
Rob spun incredible sets and the vibe was just *incredible* (this may be 
a bit biased, as my main joy in the party was to hear my own record get 
played as the sun rose :-)) You should definitely come up to Seattle 
another time and actually check out the scene.  I hope the Underground 
didn't scare you off :)

And as the The Flavor, we share an office with them just a few blocks 
from the Underground! :-)

Peace,
Matt Corwine
XLR8R Magazine, Seattle

     Shalom, Ovid!
     
        Your article from THE FLAVOR brought me out of "lurk" mode much 
     earlier than I intended, so please pardon me if I sound like the 
     newcomer to rave that I am.
     
        It's good to see the messages of nonviolence continue to spread 
     where they are needed.  Dr. King and Gandhi would be satisfied (were 
     they still functioning in this existence) to know that their 
     philosophical and moral legacies continue.
     
        As an interesting side note, I saw a broadcast of one of 
     Ferrakhan's speeches during last Christmas vacation.  [He's an 
     excellent orator -- I learned a few things watching him.]  Once waded 
     past the initial reactions and started thinking on the core of that 
     speech, I felt that he said the same:  first give yourself back your 
     mind and refuse to give it away or sell it, then the rest will follow 
     as you work to give yourself back your humanity and your dignity.
     
        My housemate is going through a much milder case of this in his 
     transformation from introvert computer jockey into a dynamic open 
     hypnotherapist.  It works -- I'm starting down a similar road myself.
     
                Joe Beckenbach

I went to a weekly last night - Kit Kat at the Endup

Acid Jazz outfit Mod Squad played for awhile and then a
DJ with a live percussion section.  The DJ was into
the less funky side of Acid Jazz.  The percussionists were
good at times and distracting at others.

They made me tuck my shirt into my pants in the name
of some abstract dress code that allows people in shorts
and goofy tassled leather shoes but not loose tshirts.

The place was packed.
It was a heavy drinking singles pick-up scene.
Only a very occasional SuperStar was to be found.

Dave

I want to thank and congratulate everone involved with Friends & Family.  
It's the best party I've been to this year.  I have just joined the mail 
list after having got the calendar a few months.  I have been trying to 
make it to all the sfraves events.  They seem to have the right vibe so 
missing at commercial raves.  I've had it with the lines, high door 
prices and yellow jackets sticking their hands in my pockets.  I was at 
the Vortex that Larry mentioned, it was similar.  Actually F&F was 
probably better.  I'm looking forward to the next one-I'll have to get 
some toys!  I went to the Apocalypse warehouse break-in a couple ov weeks 
ago.  Great idea, unfortunately a menacing police appearance at the map 
point kept people away.  The sound system wasn't up to the huge space, 
either. (It was at the huge pier 70 space that hosted SRL recently).  
It's good to see some techno breaking into this area.  So a techno theme 
for the next F&F is a great idea.  The house groove has become a rut 
around here.  I liked the Acid House theme of the last one.  Love that 
tr-303 sound.
If nothing interests you on this week's sparse list, you should check out 
Crash Worship Saturday at the dreaded Haze theater.  If you haven't seen 
'em before, you'll be amazed.  Especially if you like the nude guy.  
All I'll say about it is wear old clothes and show up about 1 or 1:30 to 
avoid the crusty metal bands opening.  

David

Hi all of you SFRavers,

Friends & Family was the first SFR event that I attended.  I can't thank
everyone enough for putting this incredible evening together.  It was just
plain fun!
I got there rather late so unfortunately I missed Laura's set but was pleased
to have met her.  Ethan was already spinning when I entered and I went wild.
 I thought he was absolutely incredible.  I think I may have told him 100
times how great he was.  "Ethan, forgive me for repeating myself but YOU WERE
INCREDIBLE". 
The atmosphere was very much ...HOT... The decor, the lights, toys and
all...and of course the "Naked Man" (I hope he is starting a new trend), was
absolutely ...COOL...
I took a very short break after Ethan's set but hopped back on the dance
floor to end Lee's Set, also very good.  Then came Alex...wow, wow, wow
again.  I've heard Alex spin in his own store "Gaia Mantra" but never heard
him Live.  He was also most incredible.  (Alex you're a genius).  By that
time I think I danced for about 4-1/2 hours and I was done for.  I wish I
could have stayed longer to listen to more djs but I guess it will have to be
for a next time.
Again thanks to all sfRavers involved.  I got to meet Laura, Brian (wired),
Cindy Kawakami (she intruduced me to many great people but I forget some
names), of course Ethan and Alex and probably a few others I forget.
This is an evening I will not forget for a long time.  Let's do it again.
Denis - JeffsHarp (ravnBird)

Subject: A Little Sultan
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU

 This is a review of a little club rave that will be happening every
Friday in Santa Clara.

 The place is actually a restaurant , not a club per se. It's the Sultan
restaurant , and they serve Middle Eastern cuisine. It's at 3099
El Camino Real in Santa Clara town - unfortunetly , the place doesn't 
have it's name in the curbside list of shops - it's a small place in
a corner , way behind the Taco Bell. The little shopping center is
located south of Calabasas and north of Kiely.

 As I walked in at about 10:30PM , I noticed what I took to be the
owners of the restaurant hanging out at the far end of the bar. Very 
un-show biz looking folks. About 10 patrons were already there , either
in the restaurant or just hanging out outside. 

 Nobody was dancing.

 The place had a middle-eastern motif - cloth hangings gave the impression
of a tent , small metal lanterns suspended by chains from the ceiling.
The dance area had been created by moving the tables out of the main room,
so there was mostly institutional-pile carpet to dance on , as well as the 
regular 10'x12' parquet dance floor. 

 An attempt was made to set a mood with some nice candles and incense.
However , the lighting was run by someone who didn't seem to be a 
professional - he had a multi-color-beam stage light that he would fuss
with every once and awhile , and a really annoying light that spun spots 
of lights in circles - the darn thing was aimed too low and into people's
eyes.

 And he had a fog machine too. ( I hate 'em )
 

 So , I and this one other guy stayed out of the way of the lights and
tried to get some dancing done in this vibe vacumn. Two couples who
gave the impression of walking in from the street danced for awhile
and left. It was dire.

 The first DJ was Alonzo - he seemed 18 or early-twenty-something. Mostly
housey stuff - too bad nobody was in much of a mood to dance, since his
set was good. The dance action seemed to pick up a bit after Harry Who
started spinning , and the dance floor finally came alive around 
midnight. Harry Who played mostly trance & techno , also put in a good
set ( Harry Who seems to be involved with Outer Rhythm Records in some
way - is it his store? ). Around 12:30 AM , Spun took over , and I and 
a whole bunch of other folks hit our peaks - excellent music!

 The lighting situation had improved by Harry Who's set - the annoying
light had been aimed higher over people's heads. The fog machine was
still being set off occasionally - too much fog for the small place,
in my opinion. ( Maybe he should rent the new water-vapor fog machine
next time ). 

 I had the feeling that the event was put on by amateurs with good
intentions. Sure enough , the gal at the door was the owners' daughter ;
she had talked them into trying this for a few fridays. She said they made
some money - that should encourage mom & dad to keep the thing going.

 I will try them again next friday ( hey - $3 and in Santa Clara sounds
OK to this south bay guy. ) , and will make another report. 

	Larry Ching/larryc@netcom.com

I was there, too. 

As per the space- I liked it- more than ample dance floor and 
seating area for the size of the crowd, relatively few 
"traffic-congested areas," food for those prone to late-night 
munching, and a non-smoking environment.

I'll agree that the lighting wasn't terrific, and, 
personally, I thought the incense somehow added to the 
heat and humidity of the dancefloor. I only caught Jason's 
set (Spun), which was good- the only problem was that he 
put the system into sonic overdrive on the console(?). 

For me, the major drawback was the vibe (there was one, but it 
was negative). While the crowd's vibe ranged from non-existent 
to somewhat positive at the end, this vibe was pretty much 
co-opted by the tension, nervousness, and anxiety 
of both the restaurant owners and their daughter, Suzanne. 

Anyone who, as a teenager, had a parentally-chaperoned 
party at their house can probably sympathize with Suzanne.
She was definitely put in the position of mediator for 
the evening. It was painful just to watch. 

When I came in at about 12:15, nobody was at the door to 
take my $3. I almost gave it to Harry, because I mistakenly 
thought he was working the door temporarily. Harry (Who) 
said he would take it if I really wanted him to, but then 
set me on the straight road- into the reataurant/club/bar 
without paying (after we conversed for a bit about our 
pets- we love them doggies!). About twenty minutes later,
Suzanne and her father started making rounds asking from 
one person to the next- if they had paid or not. this 
was to be determined by an easily-copied, pen-marked X 
on the hand, which also washed off very easily. 
I, of course, forked over the money without much to do-
despite the way it was asked of me. At this point, 
Suzanne seemed near hysteria; making criminals out 
of the patrons for something that was her and her parents' 
oversight- namely, having somebody at the door.

After she finished these rounds, she took a break outside-
where I was at the time. I talked to her a bit about being 
stressed-out and basically tried to get her to take a deep 
breath and relax a little. She explained to me that the 
one of the primary motivators for the party was money for 
her mother- I got the impression that the restaurant might not 
be doing too well. I also explained to her that positive profit 
margins and the house scene were two things that are difficult 
to couple. 

All in all- it could have been really good, and would be if 
the owners were more organized and prepared. Lastly, it
seemed that the owners were afraid of the patrons, or, 
at least not comfortable with our presence. This vibe 
is what for me ruined it- I felt unwelcome and I think 
many others did too.

The ending was definitely the best part- that was A.J. 
who started everyone asking for one more. I was 
dancing at this point- I had on a green shirt/jacket
and some black tights, black skirt, shoes.... 5'3",
and a plain-Jane bob.

It was Shoshana who started everyone chanting, " I'm yours, 
you're mine" after the final vinyl was pulled off the deck. 

Larry- how did I miss you! Willis- maybe next time?

Take care-

jocelyn

Subject: fun in LA
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

I just spent a long weekend down south and had a great time!

Thursday night I went to an ambient lounge called "Dub" where Joe Rice was 
spinning.  It was actually in a restaraunt/bar near the corner of La Brea 
and Melrose.  The actual lounge was upstairs:  candles, big couches (I took 
a nap on one), cushions, good sound.  Go if you get the chance.

Saturday night I went to "Landing," which was held at the Improv in Santa 
Monica.  Wow, garage parking for my car at a rave!  What an excellent concept!  

Anyway, I really liked Landing.  Downstairs was the dance floor: Shredder 
Sound System and green lasers and that really hard trance and borders on 
hardcore.  Oh it was wonderful, I felt like I was back in New York in late 
1992.  I've really really missed that hard sound and the complete insanity of 
the people into it -- bass bin worshipping and all.  Lots of younger guys all 
facing the speakers and making spidery motions with their hands or banging 
their heads against the bass bins.  Women sprinkled around moving like 
lightening with sweat and smiles on their faces.  This isn't some sugar syrup 
groove, it's rave-aerobics . . . no wonder I've gained 25 pounds since I've 
moved here: I used to do this two nights a week for 6 to 8 hours at a clip 
(and not on speed, either).  Man I'm out of shape!  It made me feel really 
great, and had made me vow to pull out the stops and start spinning in that 
vein again.  Peace through hardcore and all that :-).  The only bad thing
was that some guy was MC-ing a bit over Jonah's set, but he was quiet and
harmless compared to some infamous MC's like Romeo Romeo and Frankie Bones.

At 2 am Mark Gage (Vapourspace) played about a 30 minute set.  It was heavily 
based on his "Gravitational Arch of 10" suite, which is my all-time favorite 
piece of techno.  I loved it.  People danced like crazy but I was tired so I 
just sat on the stage and bobbed around.  It was trippy and spacey and full of 
weird swirly sounds.  

Upstairs (up two levels, actually) was an ambient room that would have been 
perfect except it was too hot and eventually got too loud.  But there were 
pretty oil projections (haven't seen those in AGES) and some film loops.  Glow 
in the dark toys abounded.

In between the two levels were a few vendors seeling the usual rave junk:  
fimo jewlery, t-shirts, and mix tapes.

Brian B. tells me that Landing was "average" for an LA party.  Well, if that 
was average then I'll definately go back again, because that party was on par 
with what was average back when the East Coast parties were all doing really 
well.  It was the most enjoyment I've gotten out of a party I wasn't directly 
involved with since I went to the final Back to Basics in New York last 
October.

Laura

"You can take the girl out of the hardcore, but you can't take the hardcore
out of the girl."

To: ezzevvravess <sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU>

did everyone miss the full moon or what? This outdoor was packed, packed, 
packed. We had a lot of fun, but the evening started out a bit shady. As 
we were trudging out to the site, we noticed way too many people heading 
back. We found someone we knew and asked what was going on to which he 
replied, "he just nearly got jumped by a couple guys with knives." 
oh-kee-doke. Since we were almost there we decided to just go and check 
it out for a minute anyway. I couldn't tell what was going on but there 
was definitely an agressive feel in the air (carried by the chilly winds 
from the bay). Everyone was basically standing in front of the dj 
(working off of the back of a pickup) or milling around further down the 
little jetty. I guess I've been spoiled by the friendliness of our sfr 
shindigs. At that moment, this place had none of it. 

Unfortunately, one of our drivers broke rank and took half of our group 
with her. sigh. But we stuck it out, and as the crowd began to thin and 
warm up to each other, things got much better. The site was good - plenty 
of room, parking, no noise at all to the street, but it was pretty windy 
and in full view of some prime Hunter's Point residential shoreline. 
Knowing how easily sound carries over water, I was surprised we weren't 
shut down earlier, but apparently, the cops had arrived before we did, 
looked around a bit for alcohol, and left. 

A high point was an amazing acid/techno set by Tony. Jeez, if Wicked 
let him spin a little earlier in the night, I might actually start 
looking forward to them again. meehhhh-moowwww-reeeez 

All in all, not bad. Outdoor, new location (at least to me), decent music 
(needed the SoundVision though), and 15 mins. from home. Just wish 
someone would clue Mr. Weather in on what season it is. Scarves in June, 
yuk. 

Adios, jmar.

Quotes of the night: "Say, could we have a sip of your water to... uh... 
                      swallow something?"

                     "No way man, I gotta get home. I don't wanna violate 
                      my parole..."

----- **** -----

More Sunnyvale Baylands Park information:

 Cost for a two-sectioned single large site is $130. Fee to vehicles 
entering the park is $3.00 each , so carpooling may be wise. The site
I'm looking at doesn't have a whole lot of parking next to it , but the
park does have a large parking lot near the entrance. 

 My first-choice site is located around the far end of the park. It's
located near restrooms and a cool jungle jim , and it has shaded picnic 
tables, two barbecue pits , and 25 amp electrical service ( is that 
enough for a sound system ? 25A * 110V = 2750 Watts ). The site is
right next to a nice green meadow , perfect for chilling and frisbee 
tossing and other open spaces stuff. One of the closest sites to the
park ranger's building.

 My second-choice site is their concrete "amphitheatre" - actually a large
triangular area where two park paths intersect . Nice hard flat dustless
dance area , but no tables , benches , barbacue pits , or shade. Some
grassy areas nearby . Close to the entrance and the big parking lot. 
Site fee is $50 , versus 2 * $65 for the first choice site. 
Park information gave me the impression that louder sound levels might
be tolerated there, as it's far from the other sites and close to the
Twin Creeks softball complex , which generates it's own levels of noise
anyway.

 I get the feeling that LOUD music ( Golden Gate "In The Light" ) levels
might be frowned upon , but something softer may be OK. The park folks
would take action "if other park users complain" , and since the other 
picnic sites are at least 75 to 100 yards away , maybe a little 
judicious aiming of the speakers and riding the volume slider may allow
us to have good dance music! ( Just dance closer to the speakers , and
maybe put the speakers higher than ground level? ).
 
 Keep those positive replies coming! 		Larry
