Subject: European scene report! ;)
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Date: Wed, 29 Jun 1994 15:12:02 -0700 (PDT)
X-Mailer: ELM [version 2.4 PL23]
Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=US-ASCII
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit
Content-Length: 3160      
Sender: sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

  Well, I'm back from a three week trip to the land where they have a LOT 
of good fucking dance music!  I went to a varied assortment of parties 
including: 1 Hardcore Jungle Rave (avec 3000 other persons)
           2 Trance/Acid Sessions in dark basements of London
           2 US House parties (I thought I was leaving it behind..)
  And half a dozen pubs where they played semi-mainstream dance music for 
a bunch of drunken brits :)

  I also happily returned with dozens of new tracks, a few tapes and the 
new Orb. Not to mention dozens of cool contacts..  Anyways, the report on 
all this goes as follows:

  Jungle : The Jungle scene is BIG in England. Everyone I talked to told 
me it was about to explode in the states. While I did have a lot of fun, 
and the vibe was good (except for the asshole who put his cigarette out 
on my back :P) I couldn't envision myself getting REALY into the whole 
scene.  But they did throw a good party, great sound, decent lasers and 
lights and lots of friendly people. It was also interesting to note that 
the crowd was a 50/50 mix of blacks and whites and it was almost 90% male.

  The Progressive Scene : These parties were very personal and friendly 
(lots of E's) although much smaller then the Jungle rave.  I made a lot 
of contacts and heard tons of great music.  The DJ's were usually 
'acceptable' to 'incredible' and at most of the parties there was only 
one realy great set. It took a while for people to start dancing though, 
I talked to someone who told me the people in London cant dance until 
their E kicks in. Oh well, London's never been known for its bright 
uplifting aurora ;)

  Garage and House - This was interesting because to me, Strictly Rhythm 
is often pretty boring, but to these guys, it was the SHIT! I knew I 
should of brought some of my vinyl over, but oh well.  The DJ's were 
realy good and liked to scratch and cut the tracks up, something you dont 
see very many US house DJ's doing. Again, good vibes all around and the 
people I met were realy interested in coming out and staying with me and 
spinning at some SFRaves parties!

  And some other stuff - I sampled 5 different record stores and got a 
plethora of different tracks. The store owners were usualy very cool and 
gave me promos and stuff that was just coming in. I also had a 
conversation with Billy Nasty (one of my fave Prog. House DJ's) but I 
didnt even know I was talking with him till I was told he worked at Zoom 
records and I made the connection. Anyway, he was a realy cool guy and I 
got his new tape which is not his best ever, but has LOTS of good acid on 
it. (poor quality tape however..)

  For all the people who wanted tapes - Sorry I couldn't get those off in 
time, but I have a new tape with all the new music I bought on it, so if 
you want a copy, just hollar. I can't send them to everyone though, so 
its first come first serve.  The tape has a lot of trance and 
progressive, a bit of funky house and some tweekin 303's and a Bagpipe or 
two ;)

 p.s.

 When's the next SFRaves party? Or any small, cool party? I'd love to 
play some new tunes for y'all =)

deaks@netcom.com

martin,  thanks for the info.  it'd be useful if you could add a little more:

- what is the admission price?

- what are the age restrictions, if any?
  (does no-alcohol mean all ages, 18+, or...?)

in the past we've heard of people being quite disappointed after driving some  
distance to a celebration only to find they lack dollars or years to get in.

the persistent practice of advertising parties without disclosing the price -  
neither on handbills, in email, nor on the telephone info line - feels  
manipulative to me, at least when i'm in less charitable moods.  how would  
sfravers feel about a Better Rave Bureau policy of requiring that all  
sfraves-calender listings include admission price, age restrictions, and price  
of water?  (we would not publish listings that do not disclose these terms.)

Susie asks:

>can anyone explain why "house" people were takings yellow smileys and putting
>bullets through there head and wearing these as fashion

These weren't "house" people at first.

The yellow smiley with the bullet hole through the head comes from the
now-classic comic novel, "The Watchmen," which came out in like 1986
or even earlier.  I readit a few times but don't recall the significance,
of the bullet-ridden smiley, but I remember seeing it in the book.  Fans
of the comic started wearing such t-shirts a while ago.

Yellow smileys come from way before the acid house scene.  When I was
a little kid in the 70's I remember they were everywhere and often
had "have a nice day" written by them.

Laura

There is a difference between essential information and information that
is a little more subjective. If I am going to a party, water, age and
price are key information that allow me to plan my evening. The
fact that a party is bigger or more commercial is an important fact,
but definitley not in the same class as whether there is water
(or washrooms even) at the party or not.

I think that from previous experience at Gathering parties, this party 
will cost $20.  Most big event parties cost that much nowadays.  As for 
the water question, I've never been to a Gathering party that had a lack 
of water, but water only costs a few bucks at the supermarket.  

All of you out there in computerland must remember that this is a RAVE, 
not a concert.  The difference between the two is that it is underground, 
so a lot of the information that is normally facilitated to people is not 
given.  I beleive that is done to either weed out cops, or to weed out 
people that are not ravers, and therefore would not contribute to the 
social, giving raver atmosphere.  

Anyway, the big parties are always going to be expensive, because they 
have to rent a big space and pay the djs that get new music all the 
time.  So knowing that, I would not be concentrating on how MUCH it will 
cost (if you must know, always bring $20 to cover admission, then maybe 
an extra $5 for emergencies, plus however much other money for what-e-ver 
else you might want :)), but which party will give you that feeling and 
atmosphere of a RAVE.  Don't just assume that all raves are created 
equally.  They must be put on by a promoter that cares, and people that 
care must attend.  

Fighting to keep the scene alive and healthy, 

dj fog <deepfog@cats.ucsc.edu>

hope to see you july 2nd.

Tony V Garcia <deepfog@cats.ucsc.edu> says:

>All of you out there in computerland must remember that this is a RAVE, 

>not a concert.  The difference between the two is that it is underground, 

>so a lot of the information that is normally facilitated to people is not 

>given.  I beleive that is done to either weed out cops, [...]

>Anyway, the big parties are always going to be expensive, because they 

>have to rent a big space and pay the djs that get new music all the 

>time.

i have no objection to large events (often in spaces expensive to rent, with  
big sound & expensive lighting, lots of top-name DJs, security, and so on)  
that charge a fair price.   i think everyone can understand the costs of a  
large event that are not present for a smaller one say in somebody's home, and  
most of us appreciate the financial risk that rave producers take on our  
behalf.

it's just that i can see no honorable reason for failing to predisclose price  
(this has been a consistent habit of certain producers despite repeated  
requests to preannounce prices).  what does being underground have to do with  
keeping the price a secret?  that somehow the cops will leave it alone if they  
they think it's a free party but not if they think admission is being charged?   
lots of other producers of "underground" as well as commercial events announce  
the admission cost and they don't seem to suffer for it.

the feeling i get is that some producers don't want to scare away the  
potential revenue from (stereotype warning) suburban teenyboppers who will  
pile into dad's car to "hey man let's go to one of those rave things", perhaps  
with little suspicion that it will cost $20, and water more.  once they've  
gotten psyched and driven there, they'll overcome their shock and cough up the  
bucks, whereas they might not have even gotten in the car if they knew the  
cost in advance.  apologies if i'm falsely ascribing motivations here but  
that's the only explanation i can think of.

previous email to sfraves has documented people arriving at big raves only to  
turn around and leave dejectedly if not angrily when they find out that it's  
$20/person to get in.  you could frame this in at least two ways:

1.  stupid would-be ravers - next time they'll know better.
2.  manipulative producer who could've saved some folks
    disappointment and gasoline money.

more frequently, we read reports here of folks who are disappointed when they  
arrive at an event and find age restrictions they don't meet.  wouldn't a  
responsible rave-spirited producer want to minimize these misunderstandings?
